Ningbo Industrial Bank

New Bank Building Completed, Opening Today 115

The Ningbo Industrial Bank is committed to supporting industry and developing fisheries, agriculture, industry, and commerce. Now, due to business expansion, the new bank building has been completed and is scheduled to open today. The history of the bank's establishment and the reasons for promoting its business are detailed below:

History of the Establishment of Ningbo Industrial Bank: Banking is a national economic organization that supports people's livelihoods and has a profound relationship with the country and society. Therefore, those who establish banks must embrace the spirit of serving society, focusing on supporting production and maintaining people's livelihoods to achieve the goal of cultivating national strength. Otherwise, the establishment of banks will lose its value. In the autumn of the 20th year of the Republic of China, the initiators of Ningbo Bank, in view of the increasing backwardness of China's production industries, believed that if this phenomenon was not urgently addressed, not only would the progress of the Three People's Principles be hindered, but also the national economy supporting the country's survival would face the danger of panic. Therefore, there was a proposal to organize the Ningbo Industrial Bank. The reason for naming it Ningbo Industrial Bank was not to promote a narrow regional perspective, but to gather enthusiastic people from Ningbo to support the entire industry, and to hope that people from other regions could also use local connections as a basis for unity, and work together for the development of industry, in order to seek the development of production. The bank was initiated by Yu Qiaqing, Wu Zhihao, Lin Kanghou, He Shaoting, He Shaoyu, Xiang Longdong, Xu Maotang, Zhang Boqin, Zhang Shenzhi, Wu Tingsheng, Yang Songren, Wu Zhihe, Yu Guozhen, Cao Guohua, Li Quancai, Dong Zhongxiu, Zhou Yongsheng, Chen Cuifu, and others in the summer of the 20th year of the Republic of China. A shareholders' founding meeting was convened on the National Day of the 20th year of the Republic of China. The Ministry of Finance successively issued registration approvals with the Qian Zi No. 14023, business licenses with the Yin Zi No. 108, and licenses with the Industry Department's She Zi No. 240. After several meetings of the board of directors, it was decided to eliminate various businesses similar to speculation, and to engage only in legal businesses that are beneficial to production, and to strive to implement the original intention. The third floor of the building at No. 500 Henan Road was rented as the bank's address. It started business on April 10th of the 21st year, and officially opened on June 4th of the same year. All service personnel of the bank take the bank's advocacy as the common direction of struggle, and the business has become increasingly developed. In March of the 23rd year, in order to facilitate services, the bank again decided by the board of directors to build a new bank building at the corner of Nanjing Road and Shanxi Road. In September of the same year, the construction of the new bank building was completed, and it was decided to move into the new site for business on October 1st. The bank's business operations are based on the original advocacy. Later, in order to seek external development, a remittance agency was first established in Ningbo, and then a branch was established. Shenjiamen has always been a famous fishing area, but due to economic decline, fishermen are extremely distressed, and the fishing industry is also declining day by day. The bank, based on its consistent goal of supporting production, established a branch in Shenjiamen, specializing in fishing mortgages and loans, so that fishermen would not be unable to use their labor due to economic difficulties. After more than two years of operation, it has achieved excellent results, and the fishermen are especially delighted. Recently, the bank, wanting to do a little to serve the economic countryside, specially established a branch in Suzhou and a sub-branch in Kunshan, specializing in mortgages on agricultural products such as rice and wheat. At the same time, branches have also been established in the French Concession and the Nanshi districts of this city, so that those who love and support the bank will not have to travel back and forth. It is heard that the bank's small loans for ordinary people will prevent ordinary people with steady jobs from being exploited by high-interest loans. The mortgage of national products has an indirect and profound relationship with the development of industry and commerce, and is now also being actively carried out. In the future, a national product warehouse will be established in order to serve national products to the best of its ability, so that the development of society and the country can gain considerable benefits from this. This is the history of the bank's establishment and the current direction of its business.

The Origin of Promoting Ningbo Industrial Bank (Zhuang Songfu): According to ancient times, the market was held in the middle of the day, and goods were exchanged for goods, without the so-called buying and selling of money. Since the creation of coins, the transaction of goods has changed to the substitution of money, and then to the use of paper money. This is the process of financial evolution. However, the exchange of money still takes goods as the standard, such as agriculture and fishing as the source of production, crafts as the place of manufacturing, and trade as the profession of merchants. Agriculture, industry, and commerce all rely on the injection of money. If financial circulation can be achieved, industry will naturally become more and more developed. If industry is developed, the economy of the society will naturally be prosperous, and the wealth and strength of the country can be expected. Since ancient times, economists have regarded the development of industry as the fundamental plan. It is for this reason that we and others have established the Ningbo Industrial Bank, not focusing on selfishness and self-interest as the goal, but wanting the agriculture, fishing, industry, and commerce of our Ningbo to jointly seek the development of production, and wanting to benefit China as well as Ningbo. Therefore, less than two years after opening, in addition to the Shanghai head office, a branch was established in Ningbo, and a sub-branch was established

Page 16

Fourth Sheet 116

A branch was established in Shenjiamen and Suzhou, and a sub-branch was established in Kunshan. In other places such as Hankou and Hangzhou, either a branch or an office was established. In the future, business will gradually expand, and industry will become more and more developed. This is the humble intention of us and others. Now, because the old site is narrow and insufficient for office use, we have moved to the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shanxi Road on the Great Horse Road. Fearing that all sectors of society have not yet been fully informed, we have written this preface to explain the origin.

The 20th Anniversary of the New China Bank 117

A Half-Month Celebration Starts Today

The New China Trust and Savings Bank was established in the third year of the Republic of China and was founded by the Bank of Communications and the Bank of China. It is the oldest savings bank in China, with a long history of credit and remarkable achievements over the years. In addition to the head office in Shanghai, branches and offices are located in Nanjing, Beijing, Tianjin, Xiamen, Suzhou, and Shanghai. Recently, the bank has reached its 20th anniversary, and a 20th-anniversary celebration will be held from the 1st to the 15th of this month to mark the occasion. The main anniversary events are listed below: (1) Promoting anniversary business: The bank's business has always been based on prudence, innovation, and the welfare of the people. Over the years, it has created the New China Life Savings Fund, the New China Education Savings Fund, etc., which have long been widely promoted and well-received. During the anniversary period, it is heard that three commemorative businesses will be promoted: (i) Housing Loans: The bank handles housing loan business with the aim of helping the general public solve their housing problems. Anyone who has a base and lacks sufficient funds to build a house can apply to the bank for a loan in accordance with the bank's stipulated methods, based on the principle of savings and in a trust manner, agree to repay in installments, and entrust the bank to design and build it on their behalf. The method is very perfect. At this time when the housing problem is extremely serious, the bank's launch of this business will surely be able to promote it well and benefit the society. (ii) Small-Amount Credit Loans: The bank's small-amount credit loan business has been piloted for several months and has achieved considerable results. During this anniversary period, it will be actively promoted to benefit the people. The purpose of handling this loan is to help those below the middle class who use their personality and credit as collateral to obtain opportunities for accommodating funds when they are legitimately needed. Anyone who is over twenty-one years old, has good credit, is in good health, and has a legitimate job can invite two guarantors to apply to the bank for a loan for legitimate purposes. The loan per household is limited to one hundred to five hundred yuan, with a monthly interest rate of eight percent, and a maximum of twelve months to repay in installments, which is extremely convenient for the borrower. (iii) Education Savings Scholarship: In order to encourage young students to study hard and pursue further studies, the bank has specially created an education savings scholarship. Children who have subscribed to the bank's education savings and are studying at schools registered with the Ministry of Education, the Department of Education, or the Bureau of Education, with an average academic grade of 80 or above, have the opportunity to receive a scholarship. The scholarship amount is 400 yuan per year for university students, 200 yuan per year for middle school students, and 100 yuan per year for elementary school students. (2) Giving Away Anniversary Gifts: During the 20th-anniversary period, the bank will give away innovative and meaningful gifts, the "New China Tumbler" and the "New China Small Round Mirror." Anyone who opens an account at the bank's head office, branches, and offices from October 1st can obtain the gifts in accordance with the bank's specially printed gift methods, until the gifts are given away. In addition, the bank previously held an anniversary essay contest to solicit savings plans from all walks of life. The results have been selected and compiled into a book, "My Savings Plan," which was published at the end of last month. In addition to being sold by the Shanghai Life Bookstore, a portion will be set aside and distributed to depositors during the anniversary period, it is said. (3) Holding the New China Village Exhibition: The New China Village, built by the bank on Xitiyu Road in Shanghai, is largely ready with all its equipment. Taking advantage of the opportunity of the 20th anniversary, a New China Village Exhibition will be held in the village from Double Ten Day to October 15th. In addition to exhibiting various real estate construction models, patterns, materials, and home furnishings, various models, pictures, forms, and regulations related to savings and trust will also be displayed. People from all walks of life are welcome to visit. The New China Economic Talks (three types have been published: "Individuals and Banks," "Individuals and Trusts," and "Urban Living Problems"), the family budget, and "A Page in the History of Family Finance," compiled by the bank's service department, will be widely distributed at the exhibition as souvenirs. It is also heard that, in order to facilitate visitors, the bank has printed a kind of China Merchants Public Bus fare voucher, which, in addition to being sent to all sectors of society, is welcome to be obtained from the Shanghai head office and various offices of the bank, it is said.

Public Works Bureau

Summary of the Hygiene Department's Work 126

The Public Concession’s Municipal Council's Hygiene Department currently has sections for vital statistics, infectious diseases, pathological testing, veterinary medicine, markets, sanitation, licensing, and cemeteries, as well as several hospitals. However, the nature and scope of its work are not yet fully understood. Records show that the Public Concession was established in 1843. It was not until 1863 that a so-called "filth removal section" was established. In 1870, the Police Committee suggested organizing a Sanitation Department to manage medical affairs, markets, and sanitation. Dr. Henderson was then appointed as the Medical Officer of Health, and the vaccination station was also established in 1870. However, due to opposition from rumors, very few people came for vaccinations at the time. Recently, its effectiveness has greatly increased. From 1929 to 1933, the Hygiene Department vaccinated 663,128 people. In the past three years, 632,474 people have been vaccinated. In 1876, a public slaughterhouse was initially established, and the planned filling of depressions and opening of drainage ditches also began at that time. Soon after, Locke Hospital was opened, and the management of household sewage and food supply was trialed at that time, employing a part-time medical officer. The Hongkou vegetable market was also established (currently, the Municipal Council has 17 vegetable markets). In 1898, the Hygiene Department was formally established, with Dr. Danley serving as the full-time Medical Officer of Health. Chemical and pathological testing laboratories and Pasteur examination rooms were prepared, and inspection work began. The Municipal Council also sought to increase laws to restrict crowds and mandate the reporting of infectious diseases, as well as register doctors, but the taxpayers did not agree. As a result, they could only start with education and persuasion, proceeding gradually. Between 1903 and 1906, the number of trained health inspectors tripled. At the same time, isolation hospitals, disinfection stations, and other offices were also established. Since then, progress has been slower, but this was unavoidable due to the misunderstanding and fear of the public. At that time, banning the sale of substandard food on the streets and conducting door-to-door inspections for disease prevention caused major disturbances. In 1908, plague was first discovered among the Chinese, and rat catching and inspection began (now a routine task). Many rats infected with the plague were found, especially near the docks. In 1910, there were more infected people, and preventive measures were implemented, which greatly dissatisfied lower-class people. After explanation, the measures continued. Mosquito control work also began in 1910, with a special focus on publicity and education. However, without a law to forcibly fill stagnant water, it was difficult to implement. From 1912, sixteen hygiene sub-offices were established within the concession, each staffed with one inspector to facilitate contact with the public and ease administration. Between 1919 and 1921, a detailed investigation of lung diseases among Chinese prisoners in the prison was conducted. As a result, improvements were made to prisoners' food, prison conditions, detention rules, and various aspects of preventing infection. The prisoners' mortality rate decreased from 69 to 42 within two years. After the Russian Revolution, many Russians fled to Shanghai, adding many problems to the sanitation work for foreigners. Regarding health education, there were fixed lectures for Chinese schoolchildren, with lecturers going to various schools at different times. Slogans and brochures in Chinese, English, Japanese, and Russian were compiled, revised, and distributed to the public at different times. In addition, a set of health films was produced and shown in cinemas at any time. Due to the sharp increase in the Chinese and Western population, the Hygiene Department had to be completely reorganized from 1921, adopting the latest European and American administrative systems with appropriate modifications to adapt to the environment. However, the frequent wars and unstable political situation, coupled with the government changes in 1926 and 1927, greatly affected the progress of administration. From 1921 to 1930, the collection and disposal of garbage and filth were transferred to the Public Works Department. As a result, the Hygiene Department could pay more attention to the supervision of food, milk, and vegetable markets. At this time, the instruments in the pathological and chemical laboratories were updated. The products of the laboratories, such as smallpox vaccine and rabies injections, have been promoted throughout China. In 1931, a qualified veterinarian was hired, and the supply of milk and meat inspection saw further progress. The standard of milk produced by dairies is the first class in the Orient. The Dairy Investigation Committee is also considering how to disinfect all milk for drinking. Its report will be published soon. The Municipal Council, in consultation with medical associations of various nationalities, formed a Shanghai Medical Committee in 1931. On April 1 of that year, a physician registration regulation was promulgated, and registered physicians, dentists, and veterinarians were registered, and their names, qualifications, etc. were compiled into a book and published in the gazette as a basis for recognition. The Municipal Council runs a foreign isolation hospital, a Chinese isolation hospital, a mental hospital, a tuberculosis sanatorium, a police hospital, a prison hospital, and free clinics, etc. From 1930 to 1931, a medical investigation committee was dispatched, and its report has been adopted in principle. Based on its recommendations, a western tropical disease hospital and a neurological hospital are currently planned, and the subsidies for non-municipal hospitals have also been increased. In December of last year, a new slaughterhouse was completed. The slaughterhouse can accommodate 1,000 cattle, 1,500 sheep, 300 calves, and 500 pigs. The lighting, ventilation, and comfort of the pens meet modern conditions. As for slaughter, the latest and most humane methods are used. All procedures are supervised by inspectors. The daily slaughter capacity can reach 250 to 300 cattle, 500 sheep, 100 calves, and 300 pigs. If demand is extremely high, it can be increased without affecting supervision. Currently, pig and sheep slaughtering is still done by private slaughterhouses, but the municipal slaughterhouse has prepared a full expansion. The tools will be tripled soon, and this activity will be centralized. Meat that has been inspected and is suitable for consumption is stamped with a mark. The slaughterhouse is equipped with a sick animal and waste meat disposal facility to prevent this spoiled meat from harming the public. The products after disposal can be used as raw materials for commodities. The Municipal Council has long planned to conduct physical examinations for schoolchildren. Recently, a doctor has been specially hired to start a pilot program in a Chinese elementary school. The Hygiene Department is well aware that in near-tropical agricultural areas, the sources of infection are mostly water and food. To cope with this, it is necessary to establish large-scale laboratories and hire a large number of inspectors. Although preventive measures take effect slowly, the quality of drinking water in this concession is no worse than that in cities with better conditions. Regarding other issues, the Hygiene Department believes that it is better to take an educational approach and proceed gradually than to impose strong regulations that cannot be implemented. Fortunately, due to this strategy, the general public and businesses have recognized the necessity of various sanitation methods. However, matters such as urban design, infant welfare, and factory inspection are still in the embryonic stage, just starting to collect and organize materials. However, when the time comes for effective action, they can be dealt with immediately. As for the investigation of the causes of death and the nature of epidemics, it is an ancillary task of the Hygiene Department, but attention is also paid to research. Because the public is unwilling to report, the records of deaths are difficult to be accurate. Or, some believe that Shanghai is the center of various diseases. This is because the investigation and statistics of this port are more detailed than those of neighboring areas, leading to this misunderstanding. When epidemics occur in other areas, they are not investigated in detail, or even not discovered. When they spread to this port, they are found out. Therefore, although the classification method of this port is not perfect, it also has this effect. The complex situation of the Hygiene Department in cracking down on various harmful things in large cities cannot be described in detail now. However, the duties of some sections of this department are the work of other departments in more densely organized cities, such as the laboratory doing analysis work for hospitals and doctors, and the duties that belong to national laboratories in other countries. Also, the expenses of infectious disease hospitals are all borne by the Hygiene Department.

A Visit to the Municipal Drug Rehabilitation Center 129

Well-Equipped, Drug Addicts Have No Suffering

Planning to Establish a Branch to Benefit Citizens

The Shanghai Municipal Temporary Drug Rehabilitation Center has been established for just three months, and the number of drug addicts who have been rehabilitated has exceeded 700. There are also more than 300 people who voluntarily seek drug rehabilitation. Its remarkable achievements can be seen. The center officially announced its establishment yesterday and invited people from all walks of life to visit. The details are recorded below.

A Glimpse Inside the Center 130

The center has not yet officially opened. The official opening was at 2:00 pm yesterday, without any ceremony. More than 200 representatives from all walks of life, including Xu Peihuang and Li Dachao, attended. At 2:00 pm, all visitors were served tea and refreshments by the center's director Yang Yannian, doctor Wu Liguo, and Shen Gao, section chief of the Health Bureau. They were then led to visit the drug rehabilitation wards. There are six rooms, housing a total of 108 drug addicts. There is also a medicine storage room, where doctors take turns serving. Some have been completely rehabilitated, while others are undergoing rehabilitation with the effervescent drug rehabilitation method. The drug addicts' clothing and meals are provided by the center. All the facilities are very well-equipped. The visitors were very satisfied.

Number of People Quitting Smoking 131

From July 11 to September 15, the center has rehabilitated a total of 732 people, including 618 males and 114 females. A. Age Statistics: 3 people under 20, 178 people under 30, 295 people under 40, 191 people under 50, and 65 people over 50. B. Types of Drugs: 158 people smoked opium, 186 people smoked red pills, 26 people injected morphine, 149 people used various drugs at the same time, and 213 people used mixtures. C. Occupational Statistics: 31 farmers, 368 workers, 204 merchants, 12 students, 14 soldiers, and 103 others. D. Drug Rehabilitation Date Statistics: 664 people within 10 days, 40 people within 12 days, 18 people within 14 days, 7 people within 16 days. 3 people stopped drug rehabilitation due to serious illnesses or important issues.

Russian Drug Rehabilitation 132

The center also admitted a Russian expatriate who voluntarily requested drug rehabilitation, named Jin Si guiue. He had been smoking for about 8 years, and his teeth were already charred. He had to smoke 4 qian of red pills and 120 pills every day, which cost a lot every month. He worked at the tram company. Due to economic difficulties, he once tried to quit, but after only five months, he became addicted again. Now he is determined to voluntarily request rehabilitation again. Since entering the center, his drug addiction has been completely eliminated in less than ten days. He can be discharged in two or three days. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency asked him yesterday if he had any pain when quitting drugs. Jin Si replied with a smile that there was no pain at all, and said that he would do his best to publicize after being discharged, so that all smokers could completely escape from the sea of suffering.

Planning to Establish a Branch 133

According to the center authorities, the center sees that the number of people voluntarily requesting drug rehabilitation is increasing day by day, and the temporary drug rehabilitation center is not spacious enough. Therefore, Wu Tiecheng, the concurrent commander, Tao Baichuan, the chief of the Military Law Department, and Li Ting'an, the director of the Health Bureau, are purchasing two mu of land on Qingyun Road in Zhabei to build the second branch. According to Section Chief Shen, the branch can accommodate 100 to 200 people. If the number of people is too large, management will be difficult. As for the construction date, it has not yet been decided, but the foundation has already been purchased.

Center's Funding 134

According to the center's published information on the establishment process, after the chairman of the Central Military Commission promulgated the drug rehabilitation regulations, the municipal government and the Songhu Garrison Command strictly searched for drug addicts. As the number of people detained increased day by day, in order to fundamentally rehabilitate drug addicts, Mayor Wu, who was also the Songhu Garrison Commander, allocated 10,000 yuan for start-up expenses and 2,800 yuan per month for recurring expenses, specifically for the drug addicts detained by the Military Law Department of the Garrison Command and those who voluntarily sought drug rehabilitation. A municipal drug rehabilitation center was established and handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau for preparation and supervision of drug rehabilitation matters. On June 26, work began in the detention center, first using extremely simple methods to rehabilitate addicts. Later, the Garrison Department allocated three large bungalows near Longhua as the site. Because the houses were dilapidated, in addition to the complete repair, offices, staff dormitories, kitchens, laundry rooms, etc. were added, along with sanitary equipment, water and electricity renovations, totaling 7,000 yuan. Other medical equipment, medicines, and clothing for drug addicts totaled 3,000 yuan. By the time the center's drug rehabilitation center was completed, 732 addicts had been rehabilitated.

Organizational Situation 135

The center is located at 2511 Longhua Road, opposite the Songhu Garrison Department. There are 14 bungalows, a total of 6 large and small wards, which can accommodate 100 people. There are two offices, two staff dormitories, one kitchen, one laundry room, and two toilets. Criminals and volunteers are admitted at the same time, all free of charge. There is one director, one chief medical officer, one resident doctor, one pharmacist, three nurses, one nursing student, one clerk, one general affairs officer, and one administrator. In addition to the medical personnel being responsible for the medical aspects of managing drug addicts, security guards are sent by the Garrison Command to be responsible for other surveillance matters.

Started on July 3 138

Industrial Experiment Institute Trials

Pure Bamboo Pulp Paper Sample 140

Sodium Sulfide Used Instead of Caustic Soda

Continue to Try to Make Other Paper Using This Pulp

In recent years, many paper mills have been established in the country. In addition to extracting pulp by the old method, bamboo pulp and wood pulp are mostly supplied by foreign goods, which cost a lot every year. With the Ministry of Industry's large-scale paper mill about to be established, the paper-making experiment is being actively carried out by the Industrial Experiment Institute, with the goal of recovering the rights and interests. It is learned that the institute's pure bamboo pulp, bleached and copied into paper sample, was completed the day before yesterday. Because it is a semi-industrial experiment, the paper output is very small. The bamboo pulp is cooked using sodium sulfide instead of part of the caustic soda. The cooking time is shorter than using all caustic soda, and the resulting bamboo pulp is also easier to bleach. It is estimated that 350 catties of bamboo can produce more than 130 catties of pulp. Now that the institute has successfully copied, it will continue to use this pure bamboo pulp to try to make other types of paper.

Large Amounts of Kerosene Stockpiled in China 146

According to people in the kerosene industry, the local branches of Asiatic Petroleum, Standard Oil, and Texaco have recently been shipping and stockpiling as much kerosene in China as possible, in anticipation of potential changes in China's import tariffs and to avoid high tax rates. The Guanghua Kerosene Company, the agency for Russian oil, has stockpiles totaling over one million cases in Hankou, Tianjin, Shanghai, and other ports. Asiatic Petroleum and Standard Oil each have stockpiles of over two million cases in China. August Imports Are Quite Remarkable 147

The total is 9,973,002 liters, worth 420,530 gold units. After deducting 976,130 liters that were re-exported, the net import is 8,996,872 liters, worth 352,388 gold units.

Kerosene Sales in Sichuan Suspended 148

It is also learned that Sichuan has suffered from years of internal strife and military disasters, resulting in as many as 100 types of miscellaneous taxes. Kerosene is a daily necessity for the people, so in addition to the regular tax rates levied by various provinces, an additional two yuan is added for every ten gallons. Although the oil companies in China have petitioned the Tax Affairs Department to find a way to abolish this tax, no concrete measures have been announced. Therefore, they plan to temporarily suspend transporting kerosene into Sichuan for sale.

Young Woman

Accuses Husband of Sodomy 149

Medical Examination Finds No Evidence

Court Rules Against the Plaintiff

Lu Qinchi, also known as Lu Rongsheng, a local resident living at No. 20, Anqing Lane, Huishan Road, married Xin Ruidi (19 years old), the second daughter of Xin Lizhong, who lives at No. 29, Lao Yuanji Lane, Tangshan Road, as a concubine last September, for a dowry of 600 yuan. Dongjiang Cooperative

Handling the Transportation and Sale of Fritillaria Bulbs 151

Annual Overproduction Causes Farmers to Be Unable to Make Ends Meet

Economic Stability Will Allow Direct Sales to Various Regions

According to Xinsheng News Agency, after the closure of the traditional Chinese medicine shops selling Fritillaria bulbs (象貝), the Traditional Chinese Medicine associations decided to use Qianhu (前胡) instead of Fritillaria until the Fritillaria situation is resolved. The Ningbo Association in Shanghai has called for mediation, which has not been successful. According to members of the Dongjiang Cooperative, the situation regarding the transportation and sale of Fritillaria bulbs is as follows:

Fritillaria Production and Sales: Fritillaria is produced in Zhangcun Village, Yinxian County, Zhejiang Province. Due to soil conditions, the production area is not large. The annual production is about 700,000 to 800,000 catties, and the annual sales are about 500,000 catties. In the past, there was a risk of overproduction, which led to low prices. There are 5,873 Fritillaria-producing households. Each household produces an average of more than 100 catties per year, which barely supports a family. The cost of each 100 catties of Fritillaria is as follows: seeds 40 yuan, land rent 13 yuan, fertilizer 6 yuan, labor 10 yuan, totaling 69 yuan. The Fritillaria produced by farmers is purchased by merchants, resold to medicine stores, then sold by medicine stores to pharmacies, and finally sold by pharmacies to patients. After being exploited by middlemen, the farmers' income is hardly enough to cover their costs.

Organization of the Cooperative: Farmers who grow Fritillaria realized that they were being exploited by merchants and that they could only protect their costs by collectively transporting and selling their products and eliminating the middlemen. Therefore, they spontaneously organized a cooperative. The entire amount of Fritillaria is collected and not purchased with money, and it is all concentrated together. The cooperative was formally established on March 1, 1933. In accordance with current cooperative regulations, an application was submitted to the competent authorities for approval. The Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department has assigned personnel to the cooperative to provide guidance on all administrative facilities. All proposals are decided by the General Assembly of Member Representatives and implemented after approval by the authorities. Three percent of the funds are taken from the proceeds, and the surplus is used as a public reserve. The Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department has set the price at 150 yuan per 100 catties on the market scale, taking into account both the producers and consumers. Each batch of proceeds is distributed equally among the members based on the amount concentrated. The nature of the cooperative is absolutely different from that of a business.

Current Transportation and Sales Situation: Because the cooperative concentrates the goods, it is necessary to distribute some funds to the members first. Since there are no large-scale buyers for the goods at one time, it is necessary to mortgage the goods to the bank for a loan. The bank believes that the prices of medicines fluctuate and require reliable medicine shops to guarantee the loan. Therefore, the four Ningbo medicine shops agreed to guarantee the mortgage loan for the cooperative and entered into a mutually beneficial sales agreement. This is a major drawback of the cooperative's economic control at the beginning of its establishment. However, this is a necessary stage in the cooperative's struggle. Therefore, the first step is to enter into a sales contract with medicine shops to eliminate the merchant class, increase farmers' income, and not increase the burden on patients at all. When the cooperative's economy is not controlled, it will implement the second step: eliminating the medicine shop class and directly transporting and selling to various ports. Since its establishment, the cooperative has concentrated 1,258,000 catties of surplus Fritillaria. Last year, it sold 500,000 catties, which at an average price of 100 yuan per 100 catties, totals 500,000 yuan. If this amount is distributed among 1,258,000 catties, the farmers' income is only 40 yuan per 100 catties, which is less than the cost. Even if the entire amount is sold, the profit per 100 catties is only 30 to 40 yuan.

Mediation of Disputes: The long-term cause of the Shanghai pharmaceutical industry's opposition to the cooperative this time is due to the fact that the industry association once opposed the cooperative last year. The cooperative compromised and gave them tens of thousands of catties of low-priced Fritillaria. This year, after the matter passed, they again accused the cooperative of monopolizing the market, using the excuse of reducing the burden on patients, and proposed to reject the use of Fritillaria, destroying the cooperative. After this case occurred, Tang Xunze, a cooperative specialist from the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department, and the Shanghai Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau mediated several times, repeatedly explaining the situation. However, the mediation was unsuccessful because the representatives of the association demanded a special price reduction. Those with clear eyes can see what their intentions are.

The theater order was chaotic at the time. As a result, one audience member was injured. The theater then called the police and arrested seven audience members: Li Rongxiang, Ma Guanjun, Zhu Defang, Wang Yan, Jiang Mingde, and Dai Shunyin. They were detained in the Sixth District. The theater falsely accused the audience members of stealing money. After questioning by the district officer, it was determined that the theater's unreasonable beating of people was also inappropriate. The case was adjourned pending further investigation and punishment.

Far East Hotel

Male and Female Gamblers Sentenced Separately 157

Yu A'gen, the chief Chinese detective of the Old Gate Police Department, learned that a secret gambling den had been organized in Room 218 of the Far East Hotel at No. 90, Tibet Road, with very large sums being wagered. He then ordered detectives Wang Shanqing and Weng Hongxun to secretly go there and make arrests at 11:15 PM. They arrested the owner, Wang Guilin, and 22 gamblers: Chen Lifu, Yu Jinfu, Liu Achang, Chai Afang, Fu Changqiu, Lu Jinrong, Chen A'e, Xia Mingcai, Chen Degui, Yang Xuejin, Wang Desheng, Xia Zhangshi, and others, both male and female. They seized one set of copper coins, one deck of playing cards, and gambling money. They were all taken back to the police station. The next morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu requested that they be severely punished. After questioning by the judge, Wang Guilin was sentenced to two months in prison. Chen Lifu and five others were each fined 50 yuan. The rest were each fined 20 yuan as a warning. The gambling equipment and money were confiscated.

Three People Attempt Suicide by Poisoning 158

All in Critical Condition

A traveler came to the Mengyuan Hotel on Hubei Road at around 10:00 AM on the 28th of the previous day. He was wearing a long gown made of homespun cloth and looked like a student. He claimed to be Shen Yufeng, 19 years old, from Shaoxing, and wanted to book a room. The porter led him upstairs and opened Room 331. He paid a room rate of three yuan, booked for two days, and nothing unusual happened. Until 2:00 PM yesterday, due to feeling economically pressured, he had a sudden impulse to die and secretly took a large dose of opium to kill himself. The porter noticed and quickly sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. His life is still in danger. (2) Huang Youzhang, a 27-year-old from Chongming, who used to work at the Tianlu Tea and Food Shop at the stolen chicken bridge entrance on North Zhejiang Road, committed suicide by poisoning himself at home at around 1:00 PM yesterday due to being unemployed for too long and having financial difficulties. He had an argument with his wife and became resentful. He was discovered and sent to Renji Hospital by car. (3) A young traveler came to the Ningkang Hotel on North Zhejiang Road the night before. He said that his name was Zhu Pingshan, 27 years old, and he was a businessman. He booked a small room, closed the door, and went to bed. Until yesterday afternoon, he had not gotten up. The porters became suspicious and tried to open the door, catching a glimpse of him with an abnormal complexion and incoherent speech. They reported to the Haining Road Police Station, who sent an ambulance to Tongren Hospital. After examination by the doctor, it was found that he had taken opium. He was given an injection and had his stomach pumped, and he was out of danger. He was then taken back to the police station for disposal.

Unrestrained Tram Crushes Head 160

Skull Shattered, Blood Flows

A certain number of the Shanghai Electric Construction Company's public concession trackless trams, operating on the Zhengjia Muqiao Jinghu Railway Station line, while traveling on Fujian Road (also known as North Stone Road) near Ningbo Road yesterday (the 30th) at 7:20 PM (from south to north), encountered a man of approximately twenty years old who was attempting to cross the road. The tram was unable to avoid him, resulting in him being knocked down and dragged under the vehicle. The tram wheels ran over the man's head, crushing his skull, and splattering his brains and blood everywhere, killing him instantly. The driver immediately stopped the tram and dragged the man's body from underneath the vehicle. A patrol officer arrived to record the tram and driver's details, as well as the ticket seller's numbers. They then hired a vehicle to transport the body to the Fellen Road morgue. A report was sent to the First Special District Local Court, which will dispatch personnel to conduct an examination today. A report was also made to the police chief, who will send detectives to investigate the deceased's family for verification.

Lawyers Association

Request to Reduce Service Fees 161

Regarding the issue of service fees for court documents in various courts, the Shanghai Lawyers Association noted that in some cases, in addition to the parties involved, service fees are also charged for the addresses of representatives. In order to reduce the litigation burden on the parties and the financial burden on its members, the association submitted this case to a joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members. It was resolved to submit a formal request to the Judicial Administration Department of the National Government, requesting a prompt order to all courts to refrain from repeatedly charging service fees for the same parties and their representatives, regardless of whether the documents are summonses, notices, or other documents. Committee member Zhou Xiaoan was immediately elected as the drafting committee member. The draft was prepared and submitted to the Standing Committee, which yesterday prepared a formal request and mailed it to the Judicial Administration Department of the National Government, requesting its adoption and implementation.

Except for the portion withdrawn by various banks and firms, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection covers the joint bank portion as follows: The amount issued by the bank itself and withdrawn by joint banks is 110,149,354 yuan. The reserve amount for exchange certificates for the bank itself and joint banks is 110,149,354 yuan, including 66,700,779.82 yuan in cash reserves and 43,441,474.18 yuan in guarantee reserves. The above two items, with cash reserves accounting for 60% and guarantee reserves accounting for 40%, were all checked and found to be accurate. In accordance with Article 5 of the regulations, this is a formal report. September 30, 1934, Republic of China.

Xu Wending Gong

Compilation of Memorial Articles for the 300th Anniversary of Death 164

Last year marked the 300th anniversary of the death of Xu Wending Gong (Guangqi), the Ming Dynasty's State Preceptor, in Shanghai. Scholars at home and abroad published numerous memorial articles, which were printed in national newspapers and magazines. These are truly valuable materials for those who study Wending Gong. The Shanghai Xujiahui Catholic Magazine Society has recently compiled these articles into a single volume, making it even easier for scholars to review them. The society has also re-printed Zhang Xingyao's "Brief Biography of Xu Guangqi," written in the Kangxi year of Wuwu, from the National Library of Paris and included it in the compilation. Also included are three articles from Xu's genealogy, "Wending Gong's Family Biography," which were written by contemporaries. All of the above articles are rare materials not available elsewhere. The beginning of the compilation includes multiple pages of inscriptions by political and academic figures. This compilation can be obtained from the society for a postage and printing fee of 25 cents. The society also published a special Shanghai edition of Xu last year, which is also a collection of writings commemorating Wending Gong. There are still copies available, which can be obtained for a postage fee of 20 cents.

The Guanghua Petroleum Company, recognizing the increasing number of automobiles in Shanghai, and that while there are numerous gas stations, there is a lack of fully equipped stations in central locations, has leased a vacant lot at 140 Sichuan Road, Fuzhou Road, to construct an automobile service station. After more than half a year, construction has been completed. The station occupies a large area and is fully equipped, with gasoline pumps, oiling lifts, car washing motors, parking spaces, and all kinds of automobile services. Fees are extremely low, such as parking at ten yuan per month, including services such as oiling, changing oil, and washing cars, which are cheaper than other stations. Automobile repairs are also very affordable. It is said that the company, taking a cautious approach, has entrusted the management of the station to Zhao Chunlin and others of Hualin Ji, who have extensive experience in the automobile business. The grand opening is scheduled for October 2nd.

Issue No. 29

Reading News 171

Compiled by the Reading Guidance Department of the Shenbao Circulation Library

Table of Contents

(1) News from the YMCA Reading Club

(2) Recommendation of the inaugural issue of Taibai

(1) YMCA Reading Club Recruiting New Members

The Shanghai YMCA has organized several reading clubs to encourage young people to read and develop their ability to explore issues. During the three-month trial period in the past, the members have shown a strong interest in reading, and each person has benefited greatly from mutual criticism. Now that the first phase has come to an end, new members will be recruited again from now until the end of September. Anyone who is interested in reading can report to join the club. The membership fee for this phase is only 30 cents.

Recommendation of the inaugural issue of Taibai

Among the many small publications produced under the so-called "Magazine Year," Taibai is definitely one of the most noteworthy. This inaugural issue, with approximately 70,000 words, contains 37 articles divided into sections such as "Short Essays," "Sketches," "Casual Talks," "Scientific Essays," "Customs Records," and "Miscellaneous Studies." Half of the twelve short essays are about the issue of the common language. This issue is still being discussed theoretically and is now entering the stage of concrete construction. The opinions in these short essays are also very valuable for reference. The scientific essay can be read together with the scientific essays in the back.

The "Dialect Records" in the "Casual Talks" section can be read together with the articles discussing language in the front. The articles "Remembering Mr. Huang Xiaoquan" and "Version" have nothing to do with the actual lives of ordinary people, but the remaining four articles are all very good, especially "Humorous Street Vendor Voices" and "Briefly Discussing Intermediate Readings," which are more brilliant. The former records two unnoticed details in hundreds of words, which can make people feel deeply meaningful after reading; the latter discusses the so-called "intermediate reading" publications that are neither exclusively "hard" nor purely "soft."

The most noteworthy parts of the inaugural issue of Taibai are the "Sketches" and "Scientific Essays" sections, and we can also see that it places special emphasis on these two sections. Sketches are the original form of short essays, which have been very popular abroad. Their advantage lies in using the most concise language to describe the various aspects of society. At the same time, they are also a good way to cultivate the literary writing skills of young people in general. As for the advocacy of scientific essays, in the current situation where everyone is calling for the popularization of science, it is undoubtedly very important. Now we want to move science from the foreign building to the street, so that the public knows that science is not something mysterious and that everyone has the right to enjoy it.

All six short articles in this "Sketches" section can make people feel quite satisfied. "Great Drought" and "A Jiu and His Cow" both describe this year's drought, but the materials used are different. One focuses on the record of the rural social situation, and the other focuses on the description of the life of farmers. From these two articles, which together do not exceed 5,000 words, we have already seen the various aspects of the drought. Such techniques of material selection and structure are worth noting for young people who aspire to literature. The other articles, such as "A Rickshaw Puller," "Summer Notes," and "Marriage," all use concise language to describe the details of a certain corner of society, making people feel like they are tasting olives, with a special flavor.

Scientific essays are still a newborn child in China, so the four articles here cannot make people feel very satisfied, although they are all written based on what they have seen and heard. They lack literary descriptions and can only be regarded as popular explanations of scientific common sense. This work was originally a very difficult task, and it is even more difficult in China, where science is not developed. Because if you are a true and practical scientist, but you don't have literary cultivation, it won't work. And ordinary writers do not have in-depth research on science. We know that the four authors here are already some of the most important science writers in the country. But we don't have to stop our attempts because it is not easy. We want to hope that everyone will double their efforts to make science truly popular and give short essays a new life.

In short, this publication is worth recommending to readers at the moment. Its publishing address is the Life Bookstore on Sima Road in Shanghai, and the current special price for a full year, including postage, is two yuan.

Correction: In yesterday's newspaper, on the second page of the third sheet, sixth row, the news headline, "China National Products Factory Federation Pays Attention to the Domestic Goods Exhibition," the character "National" (國) was mistakenly printed as "Day" (日). We urgently correct this error.

Sports News 174

The Central District Stadium

Groundbreaking Ceremony Held Today

Mayor Wu Personally Laid the Foundation Stone and Exhibited the Model

The Stadium is Well-Designed and Economical

The groundbreaking ceremony for the city's grand stadium, which is expected to rival those in the Far East, will be held today in the central district. At the same time, a model of the stadium will be exhibited for public viewing. The details are as follows:

Ceremony 175

This morning at 10:00 AM, the groundbreaking ceremony for the grand stadium will be held at the stadium site in the central district. Mayor Wu, Yu Hongjun, Xue Cixin, Tong Xingbai, and Shen Tongliang will all attend. The ceremony will include: (1) Opening the meeting; (2) Chairman's speech; (3) Report; (4) Speeches; (5) Mayor Wu personally laying the foundation stone; (6) Music; (7) Conclusion. The city government will also have various models of the stadium on display at the site, starting today and continuing until the 10th, from 10:00 AM to 5:00 PM daily. The public is welcome to visit.

Completion Next Year 176

Yesterday, Xue Cixin, Acting Director of the Bureau of Public Works, told reporters that the architectural design of the stadium was commissioned by the Central District Construction Committee to architects Dong Dayou and assistant architect Wang Huabin, and approved by the municipal government. Bids were solicited by the bureau in July of this year. A total of eleven companies submitted bids, and Chengtai Construction Company won the bid with the lowest price. Construction began on August 1st and is scheduled to be completed in May of next year.

Well-Prepared Design 177

Xue continued, "The design of the grand stadium is extremely innovative. The steel-concrete roof frame, traffic flow lines, dormitory layout, interior and exterior decoration, etc., can all serve as a reference for those designing stadiums elsewhere in the country. The stadium's scale, capacity, and completeness are all achieved with a budget of one million yuan, which demonstrates the designers' painstaking efforts."

Shanghai Municipal Stadium Project Overview 178

I. Origin

The Shanghai Municipal Government, considering that the city's population has reached over three million, and lacking a large-scale stadium, which is insufficient to meet the needs of citizens for physical training and leisure entertainment. Furthermore, with the establishment of the new city center, it is necessary to have facilities to impress new citizens and promote the prosperity of the area. Therefore, the construction of the municipal stadium was planned, aiming to achieve both goals at once. In the early part of the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934), the architect's office of the Central District Construction Committee was instructed to start designing. In July of the same year, the Municipal Government obtained approval from the Central Government to issue public bonds of 3.5 million yuan, with 1 million yuan designated for the construction of the municipal stadium. This is a rough overview of the preparatory process for the construction of the Shanghai Municipal Stadium.

II. Location

Since the municipal stadium must be of a considerable scale, it requires a land area of more than 1,000 acres. To avoid requisitioning private land and to save expenses, a part of the First Park in the southwest of the central administrative district was chosen as the construction site for the stadium (No. 5 in the first diagram). It is bordered by Guohe Road to the east, Songhu Road to the west, Zhengdong Road to the north, and the Qujiang River to the south. To its south are the intersection points of the Songhu, Xiangyin, Qimei, and Huangxing four main roads. To the north is the future station where the Songhu Railway will connect to the intersection of Sanmin Road and Songhu Road, making transportation convenient.

III. Project Overview

The municipal stadium includes the currently planned sports field, gymnasium, and swimming pool, as well as the future addition of tennis courts and baseball fields (second diagram), covering an area of approximately 300 acres. The design highlights are described as follows:

(A) Sports Field

The sports field (No. 1 in the second diagram) is not only for citizens' daily physical training but also for hosting school sports meets, national games, Far East Games, and even world games. The architectural form and various dimensions are mostly determined by the needs of track and field events, as well as competitions such as football, basketball, and volleyball. The site does not adopt a U-shape or circular shape but a linked shape (third diagram). If it were U-shaped, the main entrance would have to be located at the protruding end, facing the less important Zhengdong Road, which would be inappropriate. If it were circular, it would be impossible to set up a 200-meter straight track, which is needed for track races. Other design highlights have also been carefully drafted after referring to the layouts of famous stadiums in Europe and America.

The stand of this stadium occupies a total width of 175 meters (574 feet) and a total length of 330 meters (1,082 feet). The highest point of the stadium building is approximately 20 meters (66 feet) from the ground, and the height of the stand wall is approximately 10 meters (32 feet). The field area is approximately 37,500 square meters (404,000 square feet). The center is a football field, volleyball field, and fields for high jump, long jump, discus throw, Chinese martial arts, etc., surrounded by a running track of approximately 500 meters long. The running track branches into straight tracks on the east and west sides, each 200 meters long. Outside the running track, there are three tennis courts and three basketball courts on the north and south sides.

The perimeter of the stand is approximately 760 meters (2,500 feet), and the width is approximately 17 meters (55 feet), with a seating capacity of 40,000 and a standing capacity of 20,000. Its capacity is larger than that of the Nanjing Stadium (20,000 seats).

To ensure that tens of thousands of spectators can enter and exit quickly and in an orderly manner, two types of traffic routes are set up: (A) Circular traffic routes, divided into two lines. One is located outside the ticket collection points, i.e., the passageway surrounding the edge of the stadium (third diagram) and the sidewalks and roads (9 meters wide) around the outside of the stadium. The other is located inside the stadium, i.e., the 1.8-meter wide circular walkway on the stand. (B) Vertical traffic routes, connecting the circular traffic routes and the seats in the stand, i.e., the steps between each section of the stand, leading down to the passageway at the edge of the field and up to the edge of each seat. A total of 34 of these steps are set up, evenly distributed throughout the stadium, each allowing 1,200 people to pass. Tens of thousands of spectators can all exit within a maximum of five minutes. Each step is equipped with an iron pull door, so that ticket collectors can easily maintain order when spectators are crowded. (Note: The Nanjing Stadium uses ordinary rotating doors, which makes it difficult to maintain order when spectators are crowded.)

Large gates are set up in the center of the long sides of the stadium for athletes to enter and exit in formation, and vehicles can also pass through them directly into the stadium.

To allow spectators to have a view from the stands to all parts of the field, the floor slabs supporting the seats in the stands are arranged in a curved manner, and the slope continues to increase from bottom to top. The construction method is to increase the height of each floor level by 0.6 cm (1/4 inch) compared to the level below. The distance between the front and back seats is 71 cm (28 inches), so the area occupied by each seat is 45 cm (18 inches) wide and 70 cm (28 inches) deep. According to the aforementioned capacity, 20 rows of seats should be set up.

The sports field has ample accommodation, enough to accommodate 2,500 athletes to meet the needs of holding large sports events. There are also magnificent gates and lobbies, lounges, offices, exhibition rooms, visitor's offices, radio broadcasting stations, dining rooms, etc. Its complete layout is rarely surpassed by other stadiums in the world.

Two grandstands face each other east and west, specifically for the seats of special guests and newspaper reporters. Due to economic considerations, chairs are generally not provided in the stands, except for the grandstand under the flat roof on the west side.

Another special feature is the use of the space under the stands to set up shops, public toilets, and ticket offices (third diagram). The passageway around it not only helps to shield these shops from wind and sun but also provides shelter for spectators during rainstorms. According to the current plan, only half of the space under the stands is being used, and the other half is reserved for the future construction of shops, etc.

The sports field uses reinforced concrete as a frame and red bricks for the walls, with artificial stone for the outer wall, plinth, and coping. The east and west gates adopt a Chinese style and are made of artificial stone. The rest of the structure is quite simple.

The sports field has a large number of flagpoles, which are very important when holding sports events. Floodlights are set up on the field and in front of the stadium building.

The elevation and cross-section of this stadium can be found in the fourth and fifth diagrams.

(B) Gymnasium

This gymnasium (No. 2 in the second diagram) is not only for the needs of various indoor sports for citizens but also for gatherings, exhibitions, and theatrical performances.

The capacity is 3,500 seats and 1,500 standing places. Temporary seats can be added around the walls of the sports hall when necessary.

The sports hall is located in the center of the building, with a floor paved with maple wood. It is approximately 23 meters (63 feet) wide and 40 meters (131 feet) long, and can accommodate three ordinary basketball courts. For formal competitions, a larger court can be placed in the center, leaving more space on all sides (sixth diagram). The total width of the building is approximately 46 meters (150 feet) and the length is approximately 82 meters (270 feet).

The stands around the sports hall are supported by sturdy reinforced concrete beams and brick walls, approximately 11 meters (36 feet) wide, with 13 levels, each level being 66 cm (26 inches) wide and 36 cm (14 inches) to 41 cm (16 inches) high. The live load assumed during the design was 610 kg per square meter (125 pounds per square inch), and together with the static load of 120 kg per square meter (25 pounds per square foot), the total load was 730 kg per square meter.

Inside the main entrance, a staircase is set up on both sides of the lobby for spectators to reach the stands directly. Side doors and narrower staircases are set up on both sides of the back of the building for spectators to exit the building.

The three arched doors here, that is, the main entrance of the building, are decorated with Chinese patterns. The rest of the outer walls are built with red bricks, with artificial stone blocks inlaid at the top and bottom.

Entering from the main entrance is the lobby, with ticket offices on both sides. Further in is the hall, with male and female toilets and stairs leading to the stands on both sides. Further in is the passage, leading directly to the sports hall (basketball court) and the gymnasium in the back, and to the office and reception room on the side. Also, through a door on each side (D in the sixth diagram), you can reach the changing, showering, and other rooms for male and female athletes, respectively. From here, you can reach the sports hall, gymnasium, and sports equipment storage room. On both sides of the gymnasium are the kitchen and boiler room, as well as the lobby and staircases for the aforementioned side doors.

The front and rear walls of the building, above the platform, are rounded at the top, with the highest point being 20 meters (66 feet) high. The outer walls on both sides are approximately 12 meters (39 feet 6 inches) high. The roof frames are arranged in front and back rows, each 6.7 meters (22 feet) apart, and are three-hinged steel arched frames (eighth diagram), with a span (i.e., the distance between the hinge points at both ends) of 42.7 meters (140 feet) and a rise (i.e., the vertical distance between the hinge point in the center and the hinge points at both ends) of 19.5 meters (64 feet). The radius of the curve of the upper chord is 30 meters (99 feet), and the height of the side vertical rod, starting from the hinge points at both ends, is approximately 12.5 meters (41 feet).

The lighting in the sports hall and gymnasium is taken from high-angle lighting to avoid dazzling athletes. Therefore, ten fixed row windows are set up in the dome, and sixteen octagonal windows are opened on the outer walls on both sides above the stands. Also, five rectangular windows are set up on the front and rear walls above the platform. The latter two types of windows can be opened to allow air circulation. As for electric lights, they are hung under the iron roof frame.

The heating equipment in the gymnasium adopts a low-pressure system. The water condensed by the hot air is automatically returned to the boiler. The sports hall, the gym, and the ventilation system distribute warm air. The other parts directly utilize the radiation of the heat source to warm.

(C) Swimming Pool

The purpose of this swimming pool (No. 3 in the second diagram) is to provide citizens with water sports and to hold swimming competitions. The pool is open-air and surrounded by stands with a capacity of 4,000 seats. Under the stands are changing rooms, shower rooms, lounges, shops, public toilets, boiler rooms, water filter rooms, etc. A magnificent main entrance is set up on the north side of the stands. Inside the door are offices, reception rooms, lobbies, ticket offices, etc. Corridors and passages are built under the stands along the east, west, and south sides to provide shelter for spectators from rain (ninth diagram). Regarding the dimensions of the swimming pool, according to the regulations of the American University Swimming Competition, the pool surface should be at least 18 meters (60 feet) long and 6 meters (20 feet) wide. The depth of the pool should be at least 0.9 meters (3 feet) at the shallower end and at least 1.5 meters (5 feet) at the deeper end. The dimensions of this pool have been discussed with the local sports community and are planned to be 50 meters long and 20 meters wide. The bottom of the pool is spoon-shaped in the direction of the long side, gradually deepening from about 1.1 meters (3.5 feet) at one end to 1.7 meters (5.5 feet) in the center, and then steeply dropping to a depth of 3.5 meters (11.5 feet) from the center to a point 5 meters (16 feet) from the other end. This depth is stipulated by the Far East Games. )

The pool body is constructed with reinforced concrete and waterproof materials to withstand the (water pressure) when the pool is full and the (earth pressure) when the pool is empty. 725 piles are driven into the bottom of the pool as a foundation. The bottom and edges of the pool are paved with white mosaic, and the four walls are tiled with white porcelain tiles.

The capacity of this pool is approximately 2,200 cubic meters (600,000 gallons). If this huge amount of water is changed frequently, the cost will be prohibitive, and each change will take ten hours, which is also very inconvenient. Therefore, water filtration equipment is installed to turn the turbid water clear again after it leaves the pool and then return it to the pool. The cycle continues endlessly. Each cycle has five stages, namely (1) disinfection, (2) filtration, (3) entry into the pool, (4) circulation, and (5) exit from the pool. This filtration work can continue uninterrupted during the swimming season. After each disinfection and filtration, the water quality becomes cleaner.

The lighting equipment in the pool adopts the latest style, that is, strong light bulbs are built into the pool walls underwater, so that the light and water color are combined into one, forming a complete (light source), which is very pleasing to the eye when viewed at night. On the contrary, if the pool is illuminated from above with lights, the outside of the pool will be very bright due to the reflection of the water surface, but it will only dazzle the swimmers' eyes, and the inside of the water will appear dark, which will make it difficult to rescue people in the event of an accident. Therefore, the method of setting up lights in the pool below the water surface has the two advantages of facilitating swimming and rescue. It is particularly necessary to adopt this method as summer night swimming is becoming a trend. The design of this pool and its auxiliary buildings is based on practicality, but attention has also been paid to aesthetics. The gate walls are made of artificial stone blocks and are carved to show the national female cultural colors (tenth diagram). The rest of the walls are built with red bricks, with artificial stone as the plinth and coping to save costs. Looking at all the buildings in this pool, the architectural styles of all buildings are adapted to each other with the sports field and gymnasium.

Swimming pools in various European and American countries often have small pools attached, with a depth of less than 1.2 meters, specifically for children to swim. This pool has not been able to take care of this equipment due to the limited budget, which is a pity.

(D) Tennis and Baseball Fields

Tennis courts (with three courts and stands with 4,000 seats, etc.) and a baseball field (with stands with 4,000 seats) are planned to be built in the central and northwestern corners of the stadium (four and five in the second diagram). They will be built in the future and are not within the scope of this project.

(IV) Construction

The architectural designs of the sports field, gymnasium, and swimming pool were completed under the direction of Mr. Dong Da, architect of the Municipal Central District City Construction Committee, and assistant architect Mr. Wang Bin. After being submitted to the Municipal Government for approval, the Public Works Bureau invited bids in July of the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934). Among the eleven bidders, Chen Tai won the bid with the lowest price. Construction started in August, and the groundbreaking ceremony was held on October 1. It is scheduled to be completed in May of the 24th year of the Republic of China (1935).

(V) Additional Remarks

This project has many innovative points in its design, such as the reinforced concrete roof frame, the layout of the entrance and exit traffic routes, the dormitory layout, the equipment of the shops under the stands, and the interior and exterior decoration. These are all sufficient for other places in the country to refer to when designing stadiums. The fact that this stadium, with its large scale, large capacity, and complete layout, can be completed with a budget of around one million yuan, is particularly indicative of the designer's painstaking efforts.

Gan Yuan Actively Promotes Sports

Launches Women's Sports Festival 183

(Nanchang Correspondence) Gan Yuan is the source of the New Life Movement under the earnest instructions of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, and also the foundation for the revival of the nation as Chiang called it. In the New Life Movement, sports are an important factor. Because the Chinese people are physically weak and mentally listless, if we do not strive to become strong and carry out widespread and in-depth training of the masses, then the vast number of sick people will have no way to shoulder the heavy responsibility of reviving the nation, and without a healthy body and spirit, everything will become empty talk. Therefore, Jiangxi has paid extra attention to sports since last year, especially for young students. Those above middle school must be militarized, and elementary school students must be turned into boy scouts. How are the results? Due to time constraints, it cannot be achieved overnight. However, the long gowns and gowns of students in the past, those with literary qualities, now all the elementary and middle school students seen on the streets are in ant-like cloth uniforms. The appearance is already much neater. Students account for a very small number of the population. Disregarding social and public sports is not enough to talk about universalization. The Department of Education specially expanded the several tens of acres of wasteland of the Gongyuan into a sports field last year, with running tracks, volleyball courts, tennis courts, basketball courts, and other equipment, which are very complete. Moreover, it is adjacent to Hubin Park, and citizens can often become interested in participating in leisure and recreation after visiting. In the past, all sports events were handled by students, and citizens never cared about them. Since the several citizen cross-country races held last year, citizens have been talking about them with great interest, and they know that they are not just for students to play with. Because women in our country have always not known what sports are, and their physical condition is worse than that of men, the sports field has now launched a women's sports festival. In addition to women's schools and organizations, women in the city can participate freely. Now, the publicity is being expanded and preparations are being stepped up. When it opens on October 14, it should be able to attract a group of women to participate enthusiastically. When those above like something, those below will overdo it. That is, all the troops in Gan have sports facilities for training because Jiang strongly advocates sports. For example, the Fourth Army, which is suppressing the Communists at the front, also held a large-scale sports festival in Yongfeng. The development of sports fields in various counties under its jurisdiction has a grass-on-the-wind trend. However, hygiene and sports are as close as lips and teeth. It is impossible to talk about sports without hygiene. Therefore, cleanliness and hygiene are a universal social movement in the New Life Movement. The Gan Provincial Government has set up a Hygiene Department to be in charge of its affairs in order to save the declining nation. In schools, because past school doctors were like consultants in the warlord era, only eating dry salary, the Hygiene Department specially joined forces with the Department of Education to form an Education and Health Committee, responsible for health guidance, health protection, and prevention and control of infectious diseases in schools in the provincial capital. The improvement of environmental hygiene is carried out in parallel with sports, strengthening the country and reviving the nation.

A Conversation Regarding the Establishment of a National

Academic Advisory Office 191

The National Academic Work Advisory Office will be officially established soon. The news has been repeatedly published in this newspaper. The reporter recently went to the Ministry of Education to inquire about the truth. According to the person in charge of the Ministry of Education, the office is jointly established by the National Economic Commission and the Ministry of Education. Its plan was approved by the National Economic Commission in April of this year, and its purpose is to build and seek true talents. Because the construction undertakings in various provinces are changing with each passing day, and there is a great need for talents. On the one hand, there is a sigh of difficulty in finding talents, and on the other hand, technical personnel are not using what they have learned due to life reasons. The loss to the country is incalculable. Therefore, this introduction agency is specially organized to achieve the goal of assigning people to their jobs and using their talents to the fullest. Under the current situation, the task of the office can only be carried out in three aspects: investigation, registration and introduction. At present, the introduction is only for technical personnel who are needed for construction undertakings. The nature of the agency is not entirely the same as that of general unemployment relief agencies. However, the Examination Yuan, the Ministry of Education, and other government agencies have paid close attention to the future of graduates from colleges and universities above the junior college level. The reform and expansion of the examination system will be realized soon. The future of those who have received higher education will definitely be more prosperous. The advisory office will also inherit the legacy of using people to the best of their talents and gradually expand the scope of its work to find a way out for the majority of outstanding young people. However, at this time, it can only do partial work. As for the candidate for the director of the advisory office, it is heard that both the Ministry and the Commission have agreed that Cheng Zhenji, Secretary of the Ministry of Education, will also serve as the director, and Yu Tongkui, Secretary of the National Economic Commission, will serve as the deputy director.
