To Form a University Education Research Association 194

Providing Opinions on Reforming University Education

Initiating the Organization of the National University Education Association

The Shanghai University Professors' Federation held its third joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members at the China Society yesterday to discuss important proposals such as the organization of the Higher Education Research Committee and the organization of the National University Education Association. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Attending Committee Members

The executive and supervisory committee members who attended the meeting yesterday included Hu Qibing, Xu Zeyi, Tang Xuanyi, Lin Zhongke, Zhang Shouyong, Weng Zhilong, Wang Xiaodao, Jiang Zhensan, Meng Shouchun, Wu Zijing, Zhang Lixin, Song Chongren, Huang Xianzhang, Shen Pengfei, Chen Xianmo, Jiang Jianbai, Han Juemin, Xi Wangshu, Xu Sumin, Chen Gaoyong, Wang Bolun, etc.

▲Work Report

The meeting was chaired by Meng Shouchun and recorded by Xu Shangjue. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, and then each committee reported the work situation. (Document Group) (1) Held a study abroad guidance committee. (2) Sent a letter to the Second Special Zone District Court to support the Shanghai College of Political Science and Law in the debt dispute case, hoping for careful handling. (3) Replied to the Shanghai Education Association, agreeing to reform the education methods in the concession. (4) Published a declaration commemorating the third anniversary of September 18th. (5) Drafted the outline of university lectures. (Administrative Group) (1) The original address of the Association (Mainland Commercial Building) was inconvenient. After several standing committee meetings, the group was responsible for moving to No. 208, Aimaier Road, Zhonghua Arts and Crafts Society on July 1st. (2) Tried to repay the arrears of the previous session. (3) Sorted out the Association's budget案. (Investigation Case) (1) Formulated the Association's membership survey form. (2) Cooperated with the communication and publication groups to prepare the library. (3) Started to investigate the Association's members from October 1st.

▲Important Proposals Decided

(1) Proposal to suggest to the Fifth Plenary Session to reform the direction of higher education. (2) Proposal to organize the Higher Education Research Committee of the Association. (Decision) The two proposals were discussed together. (1) Wu Zijing, Hu Qibing, Zhang Sumin, Zhu Tongjiu, Chen Zhenlu and five committee members were appointed as researchers, and Hu Qibing was responsible for convening them. (2) The document group of the Standing Committee of the Association sent letters to each committee member to contribute their opinions as much as possible within one month. (3) How to proceed with the proposal to initiate the organization of the National University Education Association? (Decision) Passed, and the Standing Committee was asked to formulate a specific plan for discussion at the next joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members. (4) How to proceed with the decision of the Second Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committee Members to increase the salary of university faculty and staff? (Decision) The Higher Education Research Association was asked to pay special attention to this point, draft a concrete opinion letter, and suggest it to the Fifth Plenary Session.

▲Temporary Motions

(1) Please ask the Ministry of Education to instruct the National Academic Work Advisory Office to establish a branch in Shanghai, or entrust the Association to investigate the academic work in the area. (Decision) The Standing Committee was asked to handle it. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Municipal Council Establishes a Normal School 195

School Opens on October 8th at Yucai Public School

Training Chinese People to Serve as English Teachers

The Public Concession Municipal Council recently established a normal school, located in Yucai Public School on Shanhaiguan Road. The school will open on the 8th of this month. The nature of the school is completely different from that of ordinary normal schools. The purpose is to train Chinese people to serve as English teachers. In addition to the students from the Council's schools, qualified students from outside are also admitted. The class time is from 5 pm to 7 pm every Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday and Friday. The subjects are divided into the theory and practice of teaching, psychology, Chinese subject teaching methods, geography teaching methods, English literature, English composition, English, and translation. The tuition fee is ten yuan per subject per quarter, and fifteen yuan for two or more subjects.

The Municipal Education Bureau Revises the Municipal Small

Teaching Staff Treatment Rule Article 9 196

Principals with 24 or More Classes May Reduce Teaching Time

The Municipal Education Bureau specially issued instructions to all municipal primary schools yesterday regarding the revision of Article 9 of the Municipal Primary School Teaching Staff Treatment Rule. The case stipulates that the teaching time of principals of municipal primary schools may be appropriately reduced according to the number of classes, which has been specified in Article 9 of the Municipal Primary School Teaching Staff Treatment Rule and is being implemented. Now, the rule stipulates that there are no separate provisions for the teaching time of principals of primary schools with 24 classes and 30 classes. The more classes there are, the more school affairs there are. In order to avoid affecting teaching efficiency and facilitate school administration, the teaching time of principals of primary schools with 24 classes and 30 classes will be further reduced. Article 9 of the rule is revised and submitted to the municipal government for approval by the Ministry of Education. The revised Article 9 of the Municipal Primary School Teaching Staff Treatment Rule is copied and issued to the bureau for your information. This order is as follows. Article 9 is recorded as follows. The establishment and salary advancement standards for principals of each school are stipulated as follows: (1) A primary school with four classes may set up one teaching director, who is concurrently held by the class teacher and does not receive additional salary, but the teaching time may be appropriately reduced by 150 minutes per week. (2) A primary school with six classes shall change to set up one teaching affairs director and one training director, who are concurrently held by the class teacher and do not receive additional salary, but the teaching time may be appropriately reduced by 240 minutes per week. When there are twelve classes, in addition to reducing the teaching time by 360 minutes per week, they may also advance one level in salary. (3) A primary school with eighteen classes, in addition to setting up one teaching affairs director and one training director as stipulated in the second paragraph, may also set up one affairs director, who is concurrently held by the class teacher. In addition to reducing the teaching time by 360 minutes per week, they may also advance one level in salary. (4) A primary school with twenty-four classes, in addition to handling matters in accordance with the third paragraph, the principals may further reduce the teaching time by 120 minutes per week. Thereafter, for every six classes added, the teaching time may be reduced by analogy by 120 minutes per week, but each principal shall teach at least 500 minutes per week.

Little Western Paradise 200

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Acts as a Merchant Entering the Folk Road, Returns to Yongshou to Say Goodbye to Family, Heavenly People Arrive in Chang'an

Li Shilian exclaimed, "So poor, is there no tax collection agency?" At this time, the shop assistant brought a bowl of braised pork. Jia Duohe first picked up a piece of half-lean and half-fat pork, put it in his mouth, slurped it down, and said with a smile, "Do you know how many days it has been since I ate such a delicious taste? I am very hungry now." Li Shilian said, "Tell me, how is the official business you handled in Yongshou?" Jia Duohe said, "Is there any need to ask? If I really wanted to make some progress, I would have to live in that place for at least ten and a half months, but I couldn't stand it. Two meals a day were cold black pancakes. I thought of many ways to get a plate of chives fried with mung bean sprouts. The best thing is that there was no oil or salt in it, but some vinegar. Not only that, there were many black spots in the dish. I don't know what they were. So, I can give this dish a four-word critique, which is cold, bland, sour, and dirty. On this day, I counted it myself and only ate two and a half bites. That's all, the most embarrassing thing is sleeping at night, not comfortable at all." Li Shilian said, "Since sleeping at night is not comfortable, what else do you have to say?" Jia Duohe said with a smile, "When I say not comfortable, I mean the opposite. Like when I set up a camp bed on the kang to sleep, there is always nothing hanging or blocking me, but those fleas are especially welcoming to me, holding a dance welcoming party all night, making my whole body itchy. Moreover, these things are still the medium of infectious diseases. My heart is constantly panicked, thinking that it is best not to get an infectious disease here. On the third day, I had a burden of ten thousand pounds, but I had to put it down. I didn't want to eat that black food anymore, so I took a car from the west and returned to Xi'an." Li Shilian said with a smile, "Your behavior is wrong. The bank asked you to set up a cooperative to help the rural areas. Of course, you have to set up a cooperative in the most difficult place. How can you turn around and run away when you encounter this most difficult place?" (29)

Tao Xiaoliu is Dead 201

— Zheng Yimei

Tao Xiaoliu's death has been reported. Another member of the Southern Society of Poets is gone. His name is Mu, style name Bo Sun, and Xiaoliu is his pseudonym. In his early years, he traveled around, especially in Beijing. In recent years, he has appeared as a celebrity and county magistrate, and he has made quite a lot of political achievements. He was very friendly with Hu Pu'an of Jing County, Hu Suliang of Shanyin, and Yu Jianhua of Loudong. They occasionally wrote poems and lyrics, exchanged and sang them for pleasure. He had a liking for beautiful women and loved the pipa. He said that the pipa, with its pillars matched with jin and lu, had more than eighty-four modes, and its value in music was no less than that of the seven-stringed zither. One year, he was traveling in Shanghai. The weather was cold and the year was coming to an end, and he had nothing to do to pass the time. So, he summoned singers to play and sing, hoping to relieve his boredom. However, the people in the singing houses have been using the huqin for every song since recently, so he could not find anyone who could lightly pluck the strings. He was disappointed, and wrote a ci in the tune of "Pipa Immortal" to express his feelings: (Recalling the past, I can listen to the desolate pipa with sad tunes. Who would have thought that after throwing away the green shirt, the singing would suddenly disappear? Stop sitting and washing the tears on the sandalwood. How many times have I wasted my time with romance? As the axis turns and emotions change, the night grows late and the wine is muddy. Sorrow is shared with the cuckoo's cries. I am still in the autumn hall with silver candles, thinking of holding the fragrant, thick clothes tightly. I used to sing softly with green hair, the sorrow of Liangzhou was thorough. I left behind ten thousand years of sighs of prosperity and decline, looking forward to recognizing each other in the eyes of the setting sun. The drums and strings are broken, and I can carefully retell the story before the wine cup.) His poems also have a lot of desolate and mournful tones, probably due to the environment. As Pu'an said: (I drank with you and talked about my life. I didn't cast gold, but I cast emotions. The broken stems drift for a long time and fill the sea of regret. Writing books doesn't leave a poetic name. My heart is like water, cold as ashes. I look at people with white eyes, the candle is too bright. The most is the spring breeze blowing again, the partridge singing in the depths of the elms.) In summary, his life, poems are richer than prose, and lyrics are more than poems. I don't know if his works can be kept from being scattered. It is worth publishing a collection of lyrics to circulate.

Vase 203

— Miao Shen

The year before last, I went to Hankou and passed through Jiujiang. When I arrived at the pier, there were hawkers selling porcelain who came to the boat to peddle various kinds of porcelain. Among them was a very large vase, the color was very elegant and bright. The hawker tried his best to persuade me to buy it. I refused him and said: I have no use for such a big vase. He smiled and said: Sir, you can take it back and use it as a decoration in the hall! It turns out that this kind of large vase can only be used as decoration!

Now there are many speculative stores that use many beautiful female employees to attract customers and decorate the storefront. These old guys are not opening up female occupations to adapt to the trend; they are adapting to the psychology of the public today, using cosmetics and flesh to develop their commercial plans. Therefore, the money that female employees sell is 丨丨 of course not all parts. It is not in their academic skills, but in selling their flower-like youth. If you are old, I am afraid your position will disappear like youth 丨 So now some people compare female employees to a vase used for decoration.

A woman with high ambitions certainly does not want to accept such an insult. Isn't a vase in a store a waste in society? Moreover, being a vase is still a trick to sell youth. Isn't it enough to sigh and regret when a woman sells her youth! Women have their own intelligence and talents, why can they only be a vase? This is certainly half for the environment, but half is also because they are too obviously acting as other people's playthings. In general, female employees dress up and are extremely delicate. This is to try to make a (very elegant and bright) vase!

What is even more strange is that women recognize themselves as vases and are not surprised. A few days ago, I went to visit my cousin, Ms. Mou. She said that she was going to drop out of school this semester to work as a female employee in a company or foreign firm. I said that there is no point in being a female employee, it is better to seek more knowledge. Moreover, I am afraid that your current knowledge is not enough to be a capable female employee. She smiled and said: Then it's okay to be a vase. It can be seen that a group of women is still like (Nora) before they walked out, calling them kittens and sparrows, which is sweet as honey!

The Temptation of the Silver Box

Two Kinds of Vagrants 204

— (One)

In every small town, there are two kinds of vagrant characters, the Shaoxing boss and the Chaohu guest. They have the same characteristics of being bold, persevering, hardworking and enduring hardship, but they also have the habit of gambling and drinking wildly, and eventually people regard them as (Russians).

The Shaoxing boss has an olive-shaped boat with a pointed head and a pointed butt, three oars, and strong arms. Every day, he rows from A port to B port to carry guests. The big river is their home. The Chaohu guest has a shoulder pole, two cattail bags, and all his strength. He goes from the seaside to the town, exchanging heavy burdens for light burdens to go home! Trafficking (smuggled salt), the sea is the only source of life.

Because they have these good characteristics, they can often gain the trust of others. They can gain a foothold no matter where they wander. But because of these bad habits, they cause trouble and cannot establish a family or business. They are always and forever vagrants in every small town.

Wandering in the Arts

Opening Remarks 205

— Zhang Zhenlü

(Opening Remarks), what is called (Opening Remarks)? I think, in our country, there are always some provinces where people do not understand what "Opening Remarks" are. (Opening Remarks), is not some fashionable name like (Cashmere), it is a long-standing, authentic national essence. As the name suggests, (Opening Remarks) is the beginning of a piece, everyone understands that. However, things like the opening remarks of books and newspapers, or prefaces to special collections, cannot be called Opening Remarks, no matter how similar the meaning is. It must be a rhyming piece that begins and ends on its own, sung in the beautiful Wu dialect amidst a cacophony of sounds, and traditionally used by storytellers (so-called ballad singers) before they begin singing a full story, that is called (Opening Remarks).

Now that the meaning is clear, if we want to know the significance of the Opening Remarks, we must first mention the origins of the storyteller, so-called (returning to his parents' home), regardless of whether the statement is wrong.

Storytellers (a respectful term) have ones who tell long stories and ones who tell short stories, which is a distinction. The scripts of those who tell long stories are like historical novels, so they focus on speaking and acting, without borrowing any other assistance. The origins of long stories lie in the Song Dynasty, gradually spreading from the palace to the common people, at that time they were called historical dramas, or commentaries. In the emperor's place, so-called (face to face with the emperor), the courtiers could not avoid putting on a solemn face, naturally tending towards monotony. The scripts of those who tell short stories are ballad novels, fundamentally consisting mostly of rhyming verses, which must be assisted by string and wind instruments, so that the story told emphasizes artistry. This kind of entertainment also began as early as the Song Dynasty, when blind women plucked the pipa and sang stories, circulating in streets and alleys, which was entirely the format of telling short stories. In the poems and private records of the ancients, one can see the above situation. Emerging from the mouths of women, it was naturally charming and pleasant to listen to, and as it was passed down, although there are now many men who tell short stories, it is most appropriate to use the Wu dialect, preserving the original style.

As for when short stories are told, first singing an Opening Remark is to make a contribution to the audience, providing a special interest outside of the main story, mostly to please the emotions, or to provoke feelings. Historical novels, the scripts of long stories, have one or two poems or verses at the beginning of each chapter, which have the same intention as the Opening Remarks in front of ballad novels, both increase interest. It's just that storytellers of long stories do not have musical instruments to assist them, making it inconvenient to recite the poems alone, and it would be difficult to imitate the chanting of verses when monks release the hungry ghosts, and the poems are not as popular as Opening Remarks, so it is simply omitted.

Since Opening Remarks are set up to contribute a special interest, they naturally should not have the same meaning as the main story. As for the materials of the Opening Remarks, whether it be past dynasties, modern times, ideal realms, or utopian lands, all loyal ministers, righteous people, longing wives, laborers, as well as the vastness of the universe allowed by the subject matter of sketches, (excuse me, here comes another sentence,) the minuteness of a fly, when and where can't you find materials to make Opening Remarks? However, to construct an Opening Remark, there are several main conditions: it must grasp the material available for description and tailor it appropriately, it must describe it with extreme depth within a limit that is neither too long nor too short, it must add embellished diction to popular sentences, and it must have a unique sound that is different from poetry, song, and prose. These almost combine the strengths of poetry, song, novels, dramas, and all literary works, so creating Opening Remarks is not an easy task.

Now most short storytellers are not qualified to create their own, and the literati who are well-versed in literature inevitably despise it as a minor art and many disdain to do it, so the Opening Remarks we hear are often that batch of antiques, and many are vulgar and incoherent. Occasionally, there is a piece left by a literati, or specially made by someone for an ambitious storyteller to use, and when sung out, it feels fresh and pleasant to listen to, which is considered a rare treat for the ears. Once a new work is sung out, it is copied and sung competitively, and it is a common occurrence and not considered strange that the words are identified and recited strongly, and errors are transmitted by word of mouth.

Recently, Mr. Ni Gaofeng has been diligently creating Opening Remarks and will be publishing a special collection, and asked me to say a few words, so I have written this rambling piece.

Record of Lingering Incense 206

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

Furthermore, those two parrots were especially disappointing. Of course, I cannot deny the facts about their plumage and fail to praise its beauty. However, no matter how beautiful the plumage is, they were ultimately annoying. They simply babbled incessantly all day long, except for when we were asleep. I don't know if they were still chattering then, but whenever we were awake, we constantly heard them shouting "Long live the Empress Dowager" and "Peace to the Empress Dowager," always reciting these two monotonous blessings over and over. Eventually, almost everyone's head hurt from hearing it, and we wished we could stuff something in their mouths. However, the Empress Dowager not only didn't find it annoying, but she would always show a smile on her face every time she heard them say a blessing. No one knew what interest she found in it! Thinking about it, I couldn't help but admire Yuan Shikai even more! How good he was at catering to the Empress Dowager's psychology! Simply teaching those two parrots to say two extremely ordinary auspicious words achieved an excellent effect. Afterwards, whenever the Empress Dowager heard the parrots call out, she couldn't help but think of Yuan Shikai. In this way, Yuan Shikai's favor was naturally particularly solid!

Because this was the first time in the Empress Dowager's life that she was traveling by train, there were also four doctors on our train. Their mission, in addition to serving the Empress Dowager, was also to protect the health of our group. But fortunately, no one in our group suffered the slightest illness along the way. Everyone seemed to be deliberately provoking those doctors, never giving them a chance to show off.

Along with us, there was also a eunuch who was promoted to a very important position due to temporary needs. This person had no other strengths, he had just been a farmer by heredity, and he himself loved to study, so he had some extraordinary knowledge of botany, the recognition of various plants and trees. Shen Bao Pharmaceutical Weekly

Research and Criticism on Elephant Shell Tide 207

— Wang Qizhang

In recent days, the Dongjiang Fritillary Cooperative and the Shanghai National Pharmaceutical Industry Association have been in a major public dispute for some unknown internal reason. One side says it is to help farmers, the other says it is monopolizing and extorting prices. This is originally a kind of conflict of rights in the medicine trade. It can be said that it is a dispute over interests between wholesale and retail. It can be mediated by figures in commerce and members of the same industry. Research a compromise method, so that both parties can maintain their own rights, and it will be over. Unexpectedly, this trivial issue of price dispute between merchants has triggered a collective action by old doctors to exclude medicines. Speaking of abandoning a kind of medicine and substituting a kind of medicine, what a major issue it is in academics, and what a more major issue it is in people's livelihood. First, a small number of old doctors must never manipulate the whole country. Second, the title of price dispute between merchants must never be taken to argue and judge. Third, the society is a gathering for academic research, and the professional group is obviously different. It is even more unnecessary to join in it like a bankrupt identity and argue about the price of goods with others. I think these are all rash actions that old doctors should carefully consider. To be criticized and ridiculed by discerning people beside them, what a pity and shame it is. Here, based on my personal knowledge, this issue can be divided into several sections for research.

(1) Regarding the Issue of Abandoning Medicines This issue should be based on academics. From the past, the basis for old doctors to use medicines was the result of using people as test subjects. Therefore, the inclusion of a medicine into the canon has long sacrificed the bodies of many patients. And now when we want to abandon it, there must be a key point to criticize it, and academic proof, so that it is aboveboard. And now the old doctors, because of the price dispute of the drug dealers, in a trivial matter, advocate abandoning elephant shell, and use Qianhu to replace it. And finally, they themselves also stated (once the price of elephant shell returns to its original state, or farmers can freely sell it, a notice will be issued to resume use), clearly saying that it is entirely for the sake of price that it is abandoned, and it is entirely for the sake of price that it is substituted by other products. This is not at all the tone of a scholar, not at all the attitude of a society, and even less the original purpose of benevolent art (the patient's burden problem will be solved in the next section).

(2) Regarding the Issue of National Economy The meaning of national economy, in the past, because residents were opposed to each other, it was said that wealth gathers then people disperse, wealth disperses then people gather, and so on. But now the national economy does not take domestic groups as the object, but takes the international community as the object. Therefore, modern economists take outward development as the main focus. For example, Germany, the United States, etc., often concentrate and combine domestic similar industrial and commercial enterprises, so that domestic competition and exclusion are not allowed, and can consistently develop outward, in order to maintain the national economy and enrich national financial resources. Now the old doctors, having recognized the principle of foreign goods dumping and rural bankruptcy, why do they strongly oppose the cooperative's relief to farmers, why do they want to reject the promotion of domestic goods, and foreign goods (like American ginseng and bird's nest, etc.) are still used, without devising a way to substitute them with other products. Between patients and farmers, who is close and who is distant. The lives of fellow compatriots are not talked about in the national economy. Everyone knows that rejecting domestic goods is promoting foreign goods. Therefore, this kind of rejection is enough to (help foreign goods dump and promote the life of Chinese medicine).

(3) Regarding the Problem of the Burden on Patients It is unfortunate for a person to fall ill. In addition to the pain, the burden of medical expenses is also increased. Therefore, we express sympathy for reducing the burden on patients. However, according to the cooperative, when the selling price is less than 140 yuan per dan, the retail price of the pharmacy is 44 cents per liang. Adding this number up, it is more than 700 yuan per dan. The burden on patients is mostly in the pharmacy. According to Xu Chongdao Pharmacy, personnel must be sent to select, soak, and slice. It must be selected, sliced, and commissions must be paid. These are all losses on the work. Also, stone powder debris and stems must be consumed. Slicing must be consumed, and prices must be reduced on schedule. There must also be scale loss. Both the public and the woman are right. To be fair, there is absolutely no standard for the price of medicines in Chinese pharmacies. It can even be said that if you go to ten, there are ten prices, and if you go to a hundred, there are a hundred prices. It's not too much to say. According to their self-justification to deal with buyers, it is said that the goods have high and low quality. What is used as the standard for his high and low quality is still a big question. Therefore, the patient's burden problem is of course related to the value of the goods purchased by each pharmacy, but the real crux is probably still in the pharmacies themselves, and the conscience of each pharmacy. Just look at the increase in the number of pharmacies and the expansion of their businesses in recent years. The facts are the evidence.

(4) Regarding the Issue of Disease Treatment One medicine has one medicine's characteristics, and one medicine has one medicine's function. These are all recognized by us. Therefore, other things can be borrowed casually, but medicines absolutely cannot be confused. But when it is really unavoidable, it is not impossible to use something that is closest in efficacy. Now that elephant shell is neither out of stock, nor has any harm been newly discovered in theory, and the efficacy is not close at all, just for the sake of the drug dealers' price dispute, the old doctors will use Qianhu instead, without weighing the interests of the disease. The heart of Sima Zhao is obvious. Here, the differences in the properties and effects of elephant shell and Qianhu are summarized below for the reference of colleagues.

(A) The old doctors said that elephant shell is not found in the Compendium of Materia Medica. Later generations are accustomed to using it to treat external cold coughs. The adoption area is only in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and a corner of Shandong, etc. I think the medicinal flavors of Shennong's Materia Medica were originally only 360 kinds. Liang Tao Hongjing increased the number to double. By the Tang and Song dynasties, many more were added. In the Jin, Yuan, and Ming dynasties, 39 more were added. Li Shizhen added 374 more. According to the currently popular Compendium of Materia Medica, there are already 1,871 kinds. But there are not a few things that are not included, but are commonly used by old doctors. If we advocate not using it because it is not recorded in the Compendium of Materia Medica, then at that time, Shennong's Materia Medica only had 360 kinds. Why did later generations add so many? It can be seen that the experience medicine outside of what is recorded in ancient books is a sign of progress in medicine. If it is effective, we should add it. And the Compendium of Materia Medica clearly states (Fritillaria from Runzhou, Jingzhou, and Xiangzhou are the best. There are also in various states in Jiangnan). Although it does not specify Xiangshan, Xiangshan should be within the various states in Jiangnan. It cannot be said that it is not recorded. If it is said that it has always been filled with inferior goods from Jiangnan because of greed for cheap, then that is even more of a nonsense.

(B) There are many kinds of products that are popular in our society and called phlegm-relieving drugs. Like Polygala, Trichosanthes, Citrus aurantium, Pinellia, Schisandra, Platycodon, Ophiopogon japonicus, Tussilago farfara, Inula britannica, Gnaphalium affine, Adenophora stricta, Gleichenia japonica, Bamboo sap, Aristolochia debilis, Pumice, Mirabilite, Canavalia gladiata, Inula japonica, Aster tataricus, Stemona japonica, Glycyrrhiza uralensis, and Mori cortex, the main effect of the one kind is said to be resolving phlegm. But in fact, there are not only Fritillaria and Qianhu two kinds. However, considering its content, each has a special function. There are those that absolutely cannot be used instead. Because in the past, the thing called phlegm in our country's medicine had a very large and broad range. Generally speaking, there is phlegm everywhere in the five internal organs and six fu organs inside the body. And the so-called narrow sense of phlegm is any sticky secretion that is excreted from the oral cavity. No matter where it is born or where it comes from, it can be collectively called phlegm. Therefore, secretions from the nasal cavity, throat, etc., secretions from the trachea and esophagus, secretions from the lungs and stomach, are all mixed together and collectively called phlegm syndrome. And the medicines used are also collectively called phlegm-relieving or phlegm-resolving drugs, without any distinction. However, in past experience, the use of medicines has been quite cautious and has varied greatly. For example, Polygala and Platycodon are suitable for colds with phlegm. Pinellia and Glycyrrhiza uralensis are often used for phlegm drinking with phlegm. In fact, most of the phlegm from colds is secretions from the throat and gas. The phlegm from phlegm drinking is entirely secretions from the esophagus, pharynx, and stomach. The parts where they occur are completely different, and the secretions are different in composition. Then the medicines that treat them naturally have their own functions. Just to compare these two examples, the so-called phlegm-relieving and phlegm-resolving drugs of the past, no matter whether they treat hot phlegm, wet phlegm, cold phlegm, or qi phlegm, etc., cannot escape this reason. Therefore, the medicines that were called phlegm-relieving and phlegm-resolving in the past sometimes absolutely cannot be used instead and cannot be flexible.

(C) Can elephant shell and Qianhu be used flexibly? According to our knowledge, it can be said that it is absolutely impossible. Why? Because the functions of these two kinds are, as mentioned above, each has its own treatment target. According to the old doctor's tone, it is that the channels are different. For example, Qianhu is used in Wu Yin Tang, but not Fritillaria. Fritillaria is used in Tan Ke Hua Tan Wan, but not Qianhu. From this point of view, phlegm without coughing should generally not use Fritillaria. In other words, phlegm without coughing is not secretions from the trachea and lungs. Let's check the prescriptions of real famous doctors from the past. It can be said that there is no Fritillaria visible in the prescriptions for phlegm drinking. And there are many prescriptions for cough phlegm that use Fritillaria. Therefore, we can make a conclusion. Fritillaria acts on the respiratory system. Qianhu acts on the digestive system. The two medicines have absolutely no possibility of flexible substitution. The facts are the evidence. In the letter from Chu Huiseng to Mayor Wu, it is said that Qianhu is ineffective in treating cough phlegm. The immediate true evidence. Therefore, the old doctors, because of a small matter of price dispute in the pharmaceutical industry, lightly say that each other can be substituted without adding any research and consideration to this major issue of medicine that affects disease and concerns life. Not only do they lose their own value, but a dignified society makes a joke that misleads patients like this. It is really a great absurdity in the world. Alas. The old doctor's deterioration is evident here.

Some people say that the old doctors' desperate efforts to fully advertise for the pharmaceutical industry, intimidate, and threaten, seem to be somewhat like puppets. In fact, it is all for their own personal interests. Because the backbone figures in several old medical societies are either the owners of pharmacies or the major shareholders of pharmacies. One is two, and two is one. For personal gain, they do not hesitate to sacrifice academics, sacrifice societies, and sacrifice all old doctors, and make this unlucky and smelly trend. But according to Chu Huiseng's experience, he bought elephant shell in Minhang. Minhang is still within the boundary of Shanghai County. The effectiveness of the hive can be imagined. Alas.

Anqing Medical and Health Overview (I) 208

— Jiang Huiming

(I) Introduction

The immaturity of China's health administration and the complexity of the pharmaceutical industry have no strange shape like this in any country. This newspaper's call for articles on the medical and health conditions in various places has indeed grasped the core of a problem: in the future, we must improve China's health administration. And deeply understand the medical conditions in various parts of China. Only from this road can we gain a little harvest.

What is said here is only the local medical and health situation in Anqing. The problem is already very narrow, and the author's ability is limited, so I am sorry that I cannot write everything very precisely. Please offer this as a humble contribution.

(II) A Glimpse of Health Administration

Anqing, although it is the capital of Anhui: however, the territory is barren, and the education level of the citizens is uneven. It can be said that there is no health administration to speak of. Here, let me briefly write about the immature health situation in the local area:

Since the beginning of the Republic of China, Anqing's health administration has been under the management of the Anhui Provincial Government. At that time, the Beiyang government did not have a unified plan for health administration. Until the National Revolution

Page 22

Since the establishment of the National Government, Anqing has been administered by the Public Security Bureau of the Anhui Provincial Government, which specifically set up a Health Section to handle municipal sanitation. During this period, around the 18th year of the Republic of China, Anqing once established a municipal government, but no health bureau was established, and the Health Section of the Public Security Bureau still handled everything. Considering the past achievements of the Health Section, because the people in charge in the past had not received considerable health administration training, and some had absolutely not received medical and health education, as a result, how to improve the city's health environment, how to count births and deaths, how to carry out epidemic prevention work, how to ban wandering doctors, etc., have not yet begun.

Regarding the registration of doctors in the city, although it began in the 16th and 17th years of the Republic of China, there were many errors. The examination of qualifications, the distinction between Chinese and Western doctor registration certificates, were not emphasized. As of now, the city has registered nearly 200 Chinese and Western doctors. There are also regulations on hospital management and its registration and banning, which are equivalent to a piece of paper, and cannot be discussed.

In the 19th year of the Republic of China, when Chen Diaoyuan was in charge of Anhui, Anqing launched a city-wide health movement conference. All the local leaders dragged long brooms and participated in the parade. Unfortunately, no one has continued to hold it so far, and the citizens may have forgotten it.

Anqing's public education hall, although there is some public health work, such as reprinting small pamphlets on preventing infectious diseases in the summer, posting some health charts on the streets, holding health lectures, and launching infant health competitions, infant vaccination meetings, etc., but the actual gains are still not much.

In recent years, there is an organization of the epidemic prevention meeting in the summer, which is handled by the Anhui Provincial Department of Civil Affairs in conjunction with the major local hospitals, such as free injections of epidemic prevention vaccines, accommodating infectious patients, and setting up isolation rooms in the Tongren Hospital, which is more large-scale. All expenses are about 5,000 yuan per year, but unfortunately, it is limited by financial resources, and it is difficult to have further development. The names of the hospitals affiliated to the (Summer Epidemic Prevention Clinic) in the past years are listed below:

1. Tongren Hospital, 2. Jiansheng Hospital, 3. Boru Hospital, 4. Guangren Hospital, 5. Huimin Hospital.

(III) Business Conditions of New and Old Doctors

Anqing's society is very much enveloped in a half-new and half-old color. In terms of doctors' business, the old doctors are more developed. In recent years, with the frequent disasters of floods and droughts, the old doctors are still active in the society as usual. The reason for this is very simple: mostly because the countryside has already declared bankruptcy, the government has laid off employees and reduced salaries, and the burden of life is increasing day by day. Therefore, the general public with little property and a group of civil servants feel an unexpected deficit in the medical expenses of each family. In order to save money, they mostly invite relatively economical old doctors to solve their illnesses and difficulties. Therefore, the average monthly income of doctors who are quite famous in Anqing is about 600 yuan. The average income of middle-class doctors is about 100 yuan. As for doctors who are not well-known, they are also too pitiful. It is as difficult as ascending to heaven to have an income of 10 yuan per month.

In society, with the advancement of the times, the intellectuals among the citizens are also gradually believing in new medicine more and more. Opening a new medical practice requires some equipment, and organizing a hospital requires hiring doctors, so the expenses are more numerous than those of old doctors. Anqing's largest hospital is Tongren Hospital, which still relies on subsidies from American churches and additional fundraising to maintain it. Because the people in charge of Tongren Hospital are mostly Chinese, they can take charity to heart and do the cause of helping the poor and sick. The average number of patients treated daily is more than 200. In terms of business development and equipment perfection, only this Tongren Hospital meets the conditions of a formal hospital. The remaining private hospitals are only limited to the economy, and it is very difficult to be able to self-sufficiency in hospitals. Therefore, the presidents and doctors of private hospitals also have to seek additional part-time jobs, such as school doctors, official doctors, police doctors, military doctors, etc., to make up for everything.

Anqing is particularly lacking in pediatrics. There are often old women and sorcerers who hang up signs that they are good at treating infantile convulsions, and their business is also quite good. As for wandering doctors, monks and Taoists who write talismans and exorcise demons, new-style street performers, fox fairies, and spiritual Buddhas, etc., there are still many people who particularly believe in them. The author can only deeply sigh and say: I want to say nothing. (The End)

Common Sense Q&A about Diseases 209

— Cheng Hanzhang

(4) (10) (1) Tapeworm Category (Part 2)

(Q) What does a short tapeworm look like? What do the eggs look like?

(A) The short tapeworm is the shortest of the tapeworms, about one to four centimeters long. The eggs are covered with a thick shell, and six hooks can be seen inside.

(Q) What is the dog tapeworm like?

(A) This tapeworm is parasitic in dogs. If dog feces contaminate vegetables, it can be transmitted to humans, with the liver as an intermediate host, becoming a hydatid cyst.

(Q) What symptoms occur after a human is parasitized by tapeworms?

(A) Most of the time, there are no noticeable symptoms. However, sometimes abdominal pain, diarrhea, or constipation may occur.

(Q) What other systemic symptoms are there?

(A) There may be loss of appetite, easy hunger, general fatigue, mental anxiety, and complete loss of strength. There may also be headaches, dizziness, nausea, vomiting, palpitations, dilated pupils, irregular pulse, and convulsions.

(Q) When are the patient's symptoms most likely to become apparent?

(A) After eating salty or stimulating foods such as salted fish, green onions, chives, and garlic, symptoms are more likely to appear.

(Q) What are the significant symptoms after being parasitized by broad tapeworms?

(A) The patient exhibits symptoms of pernicious anemia.

(Q) What symptoms occur after dog tapeworms parasitize the human body?

(A) Because the dog tapeworm eggs enter the stomach, the egg membrane dissolves, and the larvae enter the portal vein and then the liver, forming a hydatid cyst. An elastic, fluctuating bulge appears on the surface of the liver, or it may suppurate and become a liver abscess. There may also be ascites, jaundice, and splenomegaly.

(Q) What is the method for diagnosing tapeworms?

(A) It involves demonstrating tapeworm segments or eggs in the stool. Segments of the unarmed tapeworm separate individually, while others remain slightly connected in several pieces. They are also distinguished by the shape of the uterus and the position of the genital pore. Eggs of the armed tapeworm are not easily found in the stool.

(Q) What are the methods for preventing tapeworms?

(A) Prevention method: All fish, beef, pork, etc., must be thoroughly cooked before consumption. All livestock or people who harbor tapeworms must be thoroughly disinfected.

(Q) When should anthelmintics be administered to expel tapeworms?

(A) Anthelmintics should only be administered after tapeworm segments have been demonstrated in the stool.

(Q) Why is that?

(A) Because anthelmintics often carry a considerable degree of risk, they should not be used in patients with suspected symptoms. In particular, they are not suitable for the weak, those with pulmonary tuberculosis, the elderly, pregnant women, or weak children.

(Q) What are the common types of anthelmintics used to expel tapeworms?

(A) Commonly used are male fern extract (maximum dose 100.0), male fern oil (10.0), pomegranate root bark (maximum dose 50.0), kosso flowers, kamala flowers, etc. (End)

A Brief Introduction to Pulmonary Tuberculosis (2) (10) (3) 210

— Hu Jiayan

Regarding the measurement of temperature, it is usually divided into three areas: oral cavity, armpit, and rectum. The most accurate of these is, of course, the rectum. Although it is slightly higher than the other two, it is generally very average. Normally, the highest body temperature each day is 37.8 degrees Celsius in the rectum, 37.2 degrees Celsius in the oral cavity, and 37.0 degrees Celsius in the armpit. Measurements in the oral cavity are often inaccurate due to prolonged contact with the teeth. If there is inflammation of the teeth or oral cavity, there will be local heat, which will, of course, lead to misdiagnosis. Measurement in the armpit is the least suitable for this disease because patients with pulmonary tuberculosis tend to sweat easily under the armpit. This evaporation of sweat just lowers the temperature, so the result is unreliable. Measurement time: 5 minutes for the rectum, 10 minutes for the oral cavity (at least 5 minutes), and 15 minutes for the armpit. Short periods of half a minute or a minute can easily lead to errors.

The important situations of increased temperature have been described in detail above, but there are also a few exceptions that are commonly seen. Normally, conditions such as hyperthyroidism, sinus suppuration, chronic appendicitis, chronic abdominal organ inflammation, and inflammation of the tonsils or teeth all have higher temperatures than usual, similar to pulmonary tuberculosis. To deal with this situation, in addition to relying on long-term reports of temperature fluctuations and precise measurement, there are also some practical characteristics of pulmonary tuberculosis itself. Although this is too trivial, everyone can test it, so I think it is worth mentioning.

First: The temperature of this disease is very easy to fluctuate. Normally, the patient's temperature is generally normal when getting up in the morning, but it will immediately rise by five or six tenths of a degree after just a small thing like rinsing the mouth first. In addition, reading and writing will also cause the same situation. Second: The temperature will, of course, change after an activity. This situation can also occur in ordinary healthy people. Needless to say, strenuous exercise will cause it, but even a normal one-hour walk can cause it to rise. However, the measurement report is below 38 degrees Celsius, which is immediately distinguishable from the disease's exceeding 38 degrees Celsius. In addition, in healthy people, the temperature can return to normal after just half an hour of rest, but tuberculosis patients need more than double that time. Third: The temperature is higher in the morning, reaching 37 degrees Celsius or higher, but this does not occur at night. This situation, which is completely opposite to the usual, is coincidentally seen in many cases at the beginning of the disease.

Based on the various pathological anatomy conditions, the temperature of tuberculosis patients also changes accordingly. Usually, chronic fibrotic processes often have no fever. Exudative types mostly show high fever or remittent fever. Consumption fever is particularly prominent when cavities occur. The temperature increase in ordinary glandular tuberculosis is generally not very severe.

Several important symptoms of pulmonary tuberculosis have now been described one by one. Finally, there is another situation that is very common, namely: The psychology of tuberculosis patients is very irritable and easily stimulated. They are easily angered by any action of others, and as a result, they almost become egoists. This is more common in women. Some patients are overly pessimistic, even in mild cases with hope for recovery. There are also those who are very optimistic and have a very strong desire for recovery. These excessive situations cannot, of course, be effective with drug treatment alone. Even very proper treatment sometimes has diminished effects. Regarding sexual desire, most patients are hyperactive. In young male and female patients, there is even a very strong inner desire to marry. This should certainly not be attempted lightly. Even if we disregard the risk of infection to the new family, pregnancy and childbirth in women are enough to make the disease deteriorate. I hope that both patients and non-patients will pay attention to this social problem. (End of this chapter)

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ears, Nose, Throat, and Eyes 211

— Tang Renjin

(10) (7) Trachoma

Regarding the history of trachoma and its impact on the country, I have already discussed it in the previous issue. We often acknowledge that it is an infectious disease, and also a contact infectious disease. This infectious bacterium has not been definitively proven even with the development of medicine today. Various research groups have been organized in Europe, America, and Japan in the East. The government has also prepared bonuses, waiting for inventors to receive them. So the proof of this bacterium may not be far away. What we already know now is that this bacterium must exist in the eye secretions (i.e., tears, etc.) of patients suffering from trachoma. It can be directly or indirectly spread to others through the medium of fingers, towels, face water, and other utensils. When there is a lot of secretion, the risk of infection is also higher. In addition, crowded living (such as prisons, schools, orphanages, barracks, factories, entertainment venues) and places with public towels (such as teahouses, restaurants, bathhouses) offer even more opportunities for transmission.

Speaking of the symptoms of trachoma, they vary depending on the severity of the disease. In the mildest cases of trachoma, patients are often unaware that they have trachoma and do not feel any pain. Sometimes, the presence of trachoma is often discovered by a doctor during a physical examination. Or, people suspect trachoma when they notice tearing, photophobia, pain, eye discharge, sticky eyelids, burning sensation in the eyes, redness in the eyes, foreign body sensation in the eyes, and blurred vision. At this time, if you evert the eyelid, you can see that the conjunctiva of the eyelid (the inner surface of the eyelid) is red, congested, and turbid, with small, oval, yellowish-gray granules scattered around. Sometimes each granule is raised, protruding above the conjunctival surface. The number of granules varies. It depends on the severity of the disease. These granules, to a certain extent, can heal and contract on their own, or be destroyed and produce scars. Or their contents soften, and the conjunctiva where the granules grow undergoes fatty degeneration or hyaline degeneration. The appearance is similar to glass or colloid, and there is a kind of luster. Clinically, there are several different names for observing trachoma. (To be continued)

Common Treatment Methods for Fever (1) 212

— Li Xing

This article discusses the treatment methods for any kind of febrile disease. The English word for fever is Fever. The word "fever" is not a specific term for any disease, but rather a condition of a disease. Many kinds of diseases cause fever. According to the principles of treatment, one should treat the disease according to its symptoms. In other words, treat the cause of the fever. If the cause is removed, the fever will naturally stop. This principle should be paid special attention to. However, fever is also extremely related to the body and must be paid special attention to. For example, a temperature above 105 degrees can easily endanger life. When Chinese people have a fever, they only know to ask a doctor to prescribe some antipyretic medicine to seek temporary relief. This mentality does not conform to the principles of modern medicine. Here, someone may ask why do people get a fever when they are sick? Now, let me use a metaphor to answer this question. We have all seen boxing matches and wrestling. Do two wrestlers generate heat and sweat when wrestling? Of course, they generate heat and sweat. Then, there is also a reason for the body to generate heat when it is sick. A febrile disease is when bacteria invade the body and the body's antibodies and white blood cells, cells, etc. engage in war. The more intense the war, the higher the fever. As a result of the war, if the bacteria win, the patient will die. If the body's resistance wins, that is, eliminates the bacteria, the disease will be completely cured. Therefore, the therapist should do their best to assist the body's resistance in this war, just as we should assist and aid our own troops to eliminate the enemies that invade us. The war in the human body must have a winner and a loser; unlike human wars, which can sometimes be mediated and resolved peacefully.

Someone else may ask, is fever ultimately beneficial to the body or the disease? Answer: Fever is beneficial to the body if it is not too high. For example, when a country encounters an enemy invasion, it will rise up to resist the enemy and do its best to drive the enemy out of the country, so that it can naturally preserve its own safety and tranquility. This is like a person having a fever. Conversely, if a country is invaded by an enemy and does not rise up to resist enthusiastically, then the enemy army will be unstoppable, and the country will be destroyed. The same is true for patients. If poisonous bacteria invade the body and the body cannot resist, the poisonous bacteria will be rampant, and the sick body will be beyond salvation. Therefore, in recent years, medical scientists have confirmed through research and experience that there is no need to be particularly afraid of ordinary fever. However, because fever greatly increases the metabolic functions in the body, we must provide the body with materials to resist. The human body is like a machine. For example, a car must use more gasoline, oil, water, etc. when it is driving fast. When a person has a fever of 105 degrees, it is like a car driving at 200 miles per hour. A person's fever is like an oil lamp. If there is oil in the lamp, the wick will not burn out, but if there is no oil, the wick will burn out. Therefore, when a person has a fever, provide him with adequate materials and place him in a suitable environment, so that the fever will not cause him special harm. Here is an example: When I was studying medicine in the United States, I had a classmate who had typhoid fever. He had a fever for a month and a half. Because he had adequate treatment, when he recovered from the illness and left the hospital, I looked at him and was very surprised. What happened? That is, he had a fever and diarrhea for more than a month, and when he was discharged from the hospital, his body was actually several pounds heavier than before he was sick. This is just an example of medicine defeating disease.

When a person has a fever of one degree (Fahrenheit), the body's metabolic rate increases by 30%. If the temperature increases by six degrees (such as from 98.6 degrees to 105 degrees), the body's metabolic rate (consumption of nutrients) will increase by one and a half times. Therefore, he must obtain this one and a half times the nutrients from food so that he can avoid damaging his internal organs.

Method of Measuring Temperature and Explanation 213

There are two types of thermometers. One is the Fahrenheit scale. The body temperature of a healthy person is 98.6 degrees. The other is the Celsius scale. The body temperature of a healthy person is 37 degrees. These temperatures are taken under the tongue. The thermometer should be placed under the tongue for three to five minutes. For children or people with mental confusion, the thermometer should be placed in the anus for three minutes. The body temperature in the anus is one degree higher than under the tongue (Fahrenheit). Sometimes, the temperature can also be taken in the armpit. This place is one degree lower than under the tongue.

The body temperature of a healthy person is 98.6. It is lower by about one degree in the morning. A temperature of 99 degrees or higher is considered a fever. Mild fevers are approximately 100 to 102 degrees. Severe fevers range from 103 to 105 degrees. At 105 degrees or above, patients often become delirious. Above 105 degrees, there is always a risk of death. People with particularly strong bodies can sometimes reach 107 degrees, but at this temperature, it is more likely to be bad than good. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Thinking for Criticism 214

— Ren Baige

(1)

Criticism is an opinion on something. A person cannot have no opinion on things, and this leads to criticism.

Moreover, criticism exists at all times and in all places.

In general, most people like to express their own opinions. If they are able to use pen and ink, then they will use pen and ink to express them in a certain form, so that they can be passed on for a longer time. Naturally, criticism exists here.

Some people, although they do not like to express their own opinions, often only let them dissipate silently in their hearts. Perhaps criticism is even more difficult to take on a certain form of expression from them, but they must have an attitude of either accepting or rejecting things, and this attitude implies at least criticism. As a result, it still cannot be said that criticism does not exist.

Therefore, we can definitely say this: Regardless of whether others acknowledge or deny it, criticism ultimately exists at all times and in all places.

(2)

However, some of our writers, as soon as they see something that seems like criticism, get angry and say: What kind of bird criticism is coming again! In their minds, the reason why criticism is bad is that it prevents writers from creating freely, and the reason why they cannot create great works is because they are constrained by criticism. Therefore, some people even invented a special "template" for critics, saying that this template is what critics often use to judge whether a work is "okay" or "not okay," as if as soon as this template is gone, they can freely create ten great works.

What is the result? The template is gone, and perhaps great works will be produced. However, another kind of thing that seems like criticism is coming again. For example, many people are asking, "Why are there no great works produced in China at present?" The premise, of course, is that there are no great works in China at present. Isn't this a big criticism? It can be seen that criticism still exists, but this kind of criticism is no longer from critics but from non-critics.

(3)

At present, we cannot deny the existence of this kind of criticism from non-critics. Moreover, we should also say that this kind of criticism from non-critics is prevalent: we can often see a kind of reading-impression-style book and newspaper criticism in all newspapers and magazines. If I meet a young man who likes to read B newspapers, then they will definitely talk about how so-and-so's work is. Also, various symposiums or tea parties and even criticism meetings are being held. This is a very obvious situation.

However, this situation may not last long. Because on the one hand, some people are already saying that reading-impression-style criticism is not criticism and do not like that non-critics also have criticism, and on the other hand, some people are scolding the shallowness and recklessness of the current Chinese criticism circles and placing themselves as exceptions as critics. This means that, it seems that the shallow and reckless Chinese criticism circles at present have suddenly exceptionally produced several very "okay" critics who make some very "okay" criticisms that pass without hindrance, but in fact, they are removing the original criticism made by non-critics as well. Because we do not believe that the currently shallow and reckless criticism circles can exceptionally produce several very "okay" critics who make some very "okay" criticisms that pass without hindrance.

Why is it necessary to remove these criticisms from non-critics as well? It can be said that each has different intentions: those who scold the shallowness and recklessness of the current Chinese criticism circles and place themselves as exceptions as critics may be doing so because they want to obtain a temporary monopoly and have not considered that they will be removed along with the criticism in the future; but some people who say that reading-impression-style criticism is not criticism and do not like that non-critics also have criticism have the suspicion of setting up a trap to make criticism re-enter the fate of a few years ago. A few years ago, were there also many so-called non-reading-impression-style criticisms from critics? I think these people may have such a move in the future: They will bestow the title of "critic" on anyone who has a bit of criticism. In this way, as critics are negated by the general public, naturally even that bit of criticism will also be negated by the general public.

(4)

Everything is inseparable from criticism. And the progress and development of everything depends entirely on the criticism within itself. Even if people do not have the courage for self-criticism, they should always have the courage to accept external criticism. Why do some of our writers get angry as soon as they see criticism?

Naturally, the incompetence of critics is a fact, but we cannot but hope that very competent critics will appear. Critics are not very competent all of a sudden. Perhaps we cannot find a bit of not-incompetent criticism among some incompetent critics, but we cannot but hope that very competent criticism will appear. Then, where do the so-called very competent critics and criticisms come from? First of all, we must understand that critics and readers cannot be separated: First, critics are also readers; Second, readers are the biggest critics. As long as we understand this point, then our writers will shake hands with criticism.

I think writers should shake hands with criticism properly. Even if the critics' criticism is incompetent, they must temporarily cherish the opinions of the general readers, and this is the reason why they must shake hands with criticism.

All very competent critics and criticisms can be asked from readers.

Bench Meal 215

— TK

Shantou, My Hometown 216

— Feier

Shantou, oh, my hometown,

Is a port without winter. The second city of Guangdong. A face of gray-black, a bottom of sin, and suffering from urban deformity.

I detest this dark city, but I also cherish this scenic hometown in the southern country.

Was it eight years ago, I was spat out of this port on a morning of turmoil and terror in an old country: And eight years later, I was sucked into this port again in a golden dusk reflected by the evening glow. Like all cities' digestion and discharge of people and goods, I was spat out and sucked in, sucked in and spat out. In a turbulent generation, a tiny person is also like a piece of wood rolled in a vortex, following the turbulence.

Although I had stayed for some time in this port of my hometown, my impression of this port is vague. I cannot know it as clearly as I know Singapore, nor can I understand it as well as I understand Shanghai.

Yet I hate this city: because it sips the blood and sweat of the farmers, and from the blood vessels of this city it transports it to the Red Hairs. Warehouses in front of customs are piled up, the laborers' voices never stop, the ships spew black smoke, and the farmers sigh in hunger in the fields.

When the world is hit by depression, mourning spreads all over the countryside, and farmers are forced to take risks. So the rich gather in Shantou, and overseas Chinese return home with capital. Land prices have risen, and entertainment venues and luxury goods have suddenly increased sharply. While the city is working hard to clear and expel the endless streams of vagrants and beggars, at the same time, the nights of Shantou are filled with the sounds of singing and gambling. Shantou's belly is empty, but Shantou's charming face cannot but be coated with powder: Shantou's legs are already suffering from softening paralysis, but the tottering torso that is propped on top of the soft legs is still full of pride. A shameful face, oh, this is my hometown!

Yet Shantou was originally not worthy of being despised like this. Look at the white waves roaring outside Mayu, but Mayu Port eternally welcomes wanderers returning from abroad with her thin mouth and cherry lips smiling. The black stones on Shi Hill are rugged, and the mountain peaks are showing a bright red smile of spring. Countless fishermen on the sea cast black nets of harvest; the paddy fields on the land are golden yellow, and in the twelfth month of the lunar year, the vast fields are still hanging with golden-red tangerines in abundance. In the golden dusk, the fields are filled with hardworking sons of the earth; in the quiet mornings, Shantou also rings with the sound of the hammers of the workers building the earth. Shantou is showing the dawn in the darkness.

Shantou, oh, my hometown!

Lonely Flower 217

— Yingzi

People are lonely, and flowers are also lonely.

Recently, my home has been so deserted that I don't even feel like thinking about flowers. A'yun thought I was too lonely and that providing some flowers to regulate the dryness of life was necessary. Appreciating his kindness, he specially sent me a bouquet of white carnations, lonely flowers.

(Lonely flowers, white carnations, a melancholic, pale girl!)

I really lack interest. Lonely flowers, let them bloom and wither lonely. Isn't my own youthful life spent just as lonely? Our world is inherently lonely! Isn't it?

I washed out a bottle to keep them in and placed it in front of the window in the bedroom, considering the matter finished. If there is a clear night with a good moon, and a quiet light shines in, bathing in the dim glow, the white carnations will secretly smile in the clear moonlight. Immersed in this淡永atmosphere, gazing at the starry night sky, a lonely blessing will faintly leak from my lips:

(Lord, have mercy on this group of lonely souls. Although they have neither joy nor suffering, do they only have to endure in this way? ······)

People also smiled as miserably as the flowers, with tears in their eyes.

The following days were all like this. Waking up with a sleepy taste, the room was filled with a wisp of clear, everlasting fragrance. Facing the morning breeze, the bouquet of carnations had already bloomed exuberantly. What a graceful summer posture, ah, summer!

Leaning against the window, let me praise this serene morning.

The church bells fluttered in the morning mist. The white carnations drooped their heads. The touch of the sun caressed them; it was like a painting of a virgin in a medieval monastery kneeling before God to receive baptism.

(Lonely flowers, white carnations, a melancholic, pale girl···········Ah!)

People age easily, and flowers fade easily. Even though they are just a bouquet of lonely blooming flowers, they cannot be allowed to possess much glory.

The flowers have fallen. ····

The pure white carnations withered and fell to the ground. The breeze flowed in from the window, blowing the fading branches and leaves, rustling with a lonely sound, a lonely flower that bloomed and withered lonely:

(The season of summer has passed.)

Sobbing, I quietly picked up the fallen petals and wrapped them in purple silk, hiding them in my pocket. I want to warm these lonely remnants with my lonely heart; there will still be a summer next year.

Small Talk Between Characters 218

— Lengmo

1. Let's Talk About the Space Between Characters

September 23rd is the old Mid-Autumn Festival 丨丨丨 The new Mid-Autumn Festival is September 15th. That method is not very clever. Not to mention there is no moon, it is not Mid-Autumn Festival at all. According to the new calendar, September, October, and November, three months are autumn. Mid-Autumn should be on October 15th. The real Mid-Autumn Festival should be the Autumn Equinox. That doesn't agree with either the old or the new method, but the old method sometimes coincides. For example, this year, inaccurately speaking, it is only short by thirteen and a half hours 丨丨丨 September 24th is the Autumn Equinox. The bustling world suddenly becomes concerned with the universe, which seems to be a good opportunity to talk about the universe.

We can take this opportunity to thank our ancient civilization. The Chinese term for the universe is much better than the Western word "Universae." Although it has been translated as the universe, its original meaning only refers to within the celestial sphere. Our universe, according to ancient sayings, is宇, which refers to the top, bottom, and four directions, and宙, which refers to the past and present. Not only is the explanation of space ingenious and lively, but it also adds time. Based on the precedent that the invention of guns and cannons should be attributed to China, the invention of four-dimensional space should also be considered China's glorious contribution 丨丨丨 Of course, regardless, few of us now understand relativity.

Actually, talking about 宙 gives me a headache. To put it simply, the distance of one light-year is one with thirteen circles of kilometers added. A 100-inch telescope can see distant space 10 million light-years away. The light from the nebula there is already 10 million years old when we see it. How to get there, we don't know. According to the theory of the expansion of the universe, assuming it moves outward at a speed of 1,000 kilometers per second, then how many eras will it take to move another 10 million light-years away 丨丨丨 The calculation is not difficult, but I don't have the courage to say how many kilometers one light-year is 丨丨丨 In short, in such a distant future, it is very likely that mankind will have long been extinct, the earth will have been completely destroyed, and the sun will be dying.

Although astronomers proudly peek into defining the universe from finite to infinite, we only feel fear about it. All we can appreciate is the quiet celestial sphere as imagined by the ancients, and a few bright celestial bodies within the celestial sphere that move regularly in the short term. We don't care about their past and present; we only care about their top, bottom, and four directions. In other words, we easily understand 宇 but find it difficult to understand 宙. 宇 is clearly presented before our eyes. We know that we are a part of 宇, while 宙 requires a lot of thought and often does not yield a result.

Therefore, I dare not talk about the universe and will only talk about the space between characters.

Mr. Township Chief (10) (5) 219

— Wang Renshu

(Then, I can only use the name of the old master to solicit donations from the village, and then I will go to Shanghai and Nanjing to run around and see; those fellow villagers will always contribute some. If the amount is not enough, then I, Dasheng, will cover it myself.)

In this way, the Chang'an Bridge, which had been broken by the flood, was repaired. Mr. Dasheng also took over the Yusheng shop from Mr. Feng Wen.

The business of Mr. Dasheng's Yusheng shop was quite good last year. Now, it is said to be a little quieter.

(The situation this year is really urgent. The price of rice is too low. Accounts can't be collected. From morning till night, there is not even half a cent of business. It's really boring to death.) Mr. Dasheng has been saying this a lot lately. And then, he added: "Rural bankruptcy, recession, economic panic, world war," new terms that the villagers didn't understand.

But the villagers didn't believe his words. Every market day, people from the upper and lower mountain villages had to go to Yusheng shop once and buy something, no matter how small.

(Don't say that. You always go to the tide temple when there's a tide. When others make a copper coin of business, you always have ten copper coins to make!)

(One family doesn't know another family's affairs; you're really chewing on maggots. Moreover 丨丨丨 again 丨丨丨) Mr. Dasheng said, plopping down on the account table. Shaking his head as if he had a whole string of things to say.

Today, while Mr. Dasheng was talking about these principles, Township Chief Mr. Feng Wen suddenly ran over again.

(What should I do? The higher-ups are urging me, and I can't hand over the people! This assignment is unbearable.) Mr. Feng Wen sat in front of the account table, distraught.

(What kind of assignment is this?) But Mr. Dasheng could immediately switch to the question raised by Mr. Feng Wen. Mr. Dasheng shook his leg and said calmly, (Tell Dongsheng to go door to door and ask; those who are willing to go, go; those who are not willing to go, pay money.)
